Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Slovak" title="Help:IPA/Slovak">[ËslÉÊÉnskÉ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sk-Slovensko.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/52/Sk-Slovensko.ogg" class="internal" title="Sk-Slovensko.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the <b>Slovak Republic</b> (Slovak: <i lang="sk">SlovenskÃ¡ republika</i>, <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" class="internal" title="Sk-SlovenskÃ¡ republika.ogg">listen</a></span>&nbsp;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>Â·<a href="/wiki/File:Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" title="File:Sk-SlovenskÃ¡ republika.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> to the northwest. Slovakia's mostly mountainous territory spans about 49,000 square kilometres (19,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), with a population of over 5.4 million. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, and the second-largest city is <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="KoÅ¡ice">KoÅ¡ice</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> arrived in the territory of present-day Slovakia in the 5th and 6th centuries. In the 7th century, they played a significant role in the creation of <a href="/wiki/Samo%27s_Empire" title="Samo's Empire">Samo's Empire</a>. In the 9th century, they established the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">Principality of Nitra</a>, which was later conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Principality of Moravia</a> to establish <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>. In the 10th century, after the dissolution of Great Moravia, the territory was integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Hungary" title="Principality of Hungary">Principality of Hungary</a>, which would then become the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> in 1000.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1241 and 1242, after the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongol invasion of Europe</a>, much of the territory was destroyed. The area was recovered largely thanks to <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_IV_of_Hungary" title="BÃ©la IV of Hungary">BÃ©la IV of Hungary</a>, who also settled <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Germans" title="Carpathian Germans">Germans</a>, leading them to become an important ethnic group in the area, especially in what are today parts of <a href="/wiki/Hauerland" title="Hauerland">central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zipser_Germans" title="Zipser Germans">eastern</a> Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, the state of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> was established. The (First) <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939â1945)">Slovak Republic</a> existed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as a partially-recognized <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. At the end of World War II, Czechoslovakia was re-established as an independent country. After a <a href="/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1948 Czechoslovak coup d'Ã©tat">coup in 1948</a>, Czechoslovakia came under <a href="/wiki/History_of_Czechoslovakia_(1948%E2%80%931989)" title="History of Czechoslovakia (1948â1989)">communist administration</a>, and became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>. Attempts to <a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_a_human_face" title="Socialism with a human face">liberalize communism</a> in Czechoslovakia culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a>, which was crushed by the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia</a> in August 1968. In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> peacefully ended the Communist rule in Czechoslovakia. Slovakia became an independent state on 1 January 1993 after the peaceful <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">dissolution of Czechoslovakia</a>, sometimes known as the Velvet Divorce. </p>
      <p>Slovakia is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>, with an advanced <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a>, ranking very high in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. It also performs favourably in measurements of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">civil liberties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">press freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_and_surveillance_by_country" title="Internet censorship and surveillance by country">internet freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">democratic governance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">peacefulness</a>. The country maintains a combination of a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> with a comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">social security</a> system, providing citizens with a <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a>, and one of the longest paid <a href="/wiki/Parental_leave" title="Parental leave">parental leaves</a> in the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Slovakia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, as well as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the OECD, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="VisegrÃ¡d Group">VisegrÃ¡d Group</a>. It is the world's largest per-capita car producer, with a total of 1.1 million cars manufactured in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-spectator.sme.sk_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spectator.sme.sk-14">[14]</a></sup> which represents 43% of its total industrial output. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Slovakia's name in theory means the âLand of the Slavsâ (<i><a href="/wiki/Slovensko" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovensko">Slovensko</a></i> in Slovak language, stemming from the older form <i>Sloven/Slovienin</i>). As such, it is a cognate of the words <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a>. In medieval Latin, German sources and even some Slavic sources, the same name has often been used for Slovaks, Slovenes, Slavonians and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> in general. </p>
      <p>According to one of the theories, between 13th and 14th century a new form of national name formed for the ancestors of the Slovaks, possibly due to foreign influence â the <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> word <i>SlovÃ¡k</i> (in medieval sources from 1291 onward<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-15">[15]</a></sup>). This form slowly replaced the name for the male members of the community, but the female name (<i>Slovenka</i>), reference to the lands inhabited (<i>Slovensko</i>) and the name of the language (<i>slovenÄina</i>) all remained the same, with their base in the older form (compare to Slovenian counterparts). Most foreign translations tends to stem from this newer form (<i>Slovakia</i> in English, <i>Slowakei</i> in German, <i>Slovaquie</i> in French, etc.). </p>
      <p>In medieval Latin sources, terms Slavus, Slavonia or Slavorum (and more variants, from as early as 1029<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-15">[15]</a></sup>) has been used for them. </p>
      <p>In German sources, names for the Slovak lands were Windenland or Windishen landen (early 15th century<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>), later also the form âSlovakia, Schlowakeiâ starts to appear (from 16th century<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>). The present Slovak form â<i>Slovensko</i>â is first attested in the year 1675.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Slovakia" title="History of Slovakia">History of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moravianska_venusa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Moravianska_venusa.jpg/200px-Moravianska_venusa.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Moravianska_venusa.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moravianska_venusa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Moravany_Venus" class="mw-redirect" title="Moravany Venus">Venus</a> from <a href="/wiki/Moravany_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="Moravany nad VÃ¡hom">Moravany nad VÃ¡hom</a>, which dates back to 22,800 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The oldest surviving human artefacts from Slovakia are found near <a href="/wiki/Nov%C3%A9_Mesto_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="NovÃ© Mesto nad VÃ¡hom">NovÃ© Mesto nad VÃ¡hom</a> and are dated at 270,000&nbsp;BCE, in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Early Paleolithic</a> era. These ancient tools, made by the <a href="/wiki/Clactonian" title="Clactonian">Clactonian</a> technique, bear witness to the ancient habitation of Slovakia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Other <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tools</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> era (200,000â80,000&nbsp;BCE) come from the PrÃ©vÃ´t (PrepoÅ¡tskÃ¡) cave in <a href="/wiki/Bojnice" title="Bojnice">Bojnice</a> and from other nearby sites.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The most important discovery from that era is a <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_skull" class="mw-redirect" title="Human skull">cranium</a> (c. 200,000 BCE), discovered near <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A1novce" title="GÃ¡novce">GÃ¡novce</a>, a village in northern Slovakia. </p>
      <p>Archaeologists have found prehistoric human skeletons in the region, as well as numerous objects and vestiges of the <a href="/wiki/Gravettian" title="Gravettian">Gravettian</a> culture, principally in the river valleys of <a href="/wiki/Nitra_(river)" title="Nitra (river)">Nitra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hron" title="Hron">Hron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipe%C4%BE" title="IpeÄ¾">IpeÄ¾</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="VÃ¡h">VÃ¡h</a> and as far as the city of <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Å½ilina">Å½ilina</a>, and near the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Vihorlat_Mountains" title="Vihorlat Mountains">Vihorlat</a>, Inovec, and <a href="/wiki/Tribe%C4%8D" title="TribeÄ">TribeÄ</a> mountains, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Myjava" title="Myjava">Myjava</a> Mountains. The most well-known finds include the oldest female statue made of <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">mammoth</a> bone (22,800&nbsp;BCE), the famous <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Moravany" title="Venus of Moravany">Venus of Moravany</a>. The statue was found in the 1940s in <a href="/wiki/Moravany_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="Moravany nad VÃ¡hom">Moravany nad VÃ¡hom</a> near <a href="/wiki/Pie%C5%A1%C5%A5any" title="PieÅ¡Å¥any">PieÅ¡Å¥any</a>. Numerous necklaces made of shells from Cypraca thermophile <a href="/wiki/Gastropoda" title="Gastropoda">gastropods</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary" title="Tertiary">Tertiary</a> period have come from the sites of ZÃ¡kovskÃ¡, Podkovice, Hubina, and RadoÅ¡ina. These findings provide the most ancient evidence of commercial exchanges carried out between the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">Bronze Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bronze Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, the geographical territory of modern-day Slovakia went through three stages of development, stretching from 2000 to 800&nbsp;BCE. Major cultural, economic, and political development can be attributed to the significant growth in production of copper, especially in central Slovakia (for example in <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0pania_Dolina" title="Å pania Dolina">Å pania Dolina</a>) and northwest Slovakia. Copper became a stable source of prosperity for the local population. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Web_Biatec.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/220px-Web_Biatec.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/330px-Web_Biatec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/440px-Web_Biatec.jpg 2x" data-file-width="824" data-file-height="408"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Web_Biatec.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Left: a <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Biatec" title="Biatec">Biatec</a> coin
         <br>Right: five <a href="/wiki/Slovak_koruna" title="Slovak koruna">Slovak crowns</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the disappearance of the Äakany and <a href="/wiki/Velatice" title="Velatice">Velatice</a> cultures, the <a href="/wiki/Lusatian_culture" title="Lusatian culture">Lusatian</a> people expanded building of strong and complex fortifications, with the large permanent buildings and administrative centres. Excavations of Lusatian <a href="/wiki/Hillfort" title="Hillfort">hill forts</a> document the substantial development of trade and agriculture at that period. The richness and diversity of tombs increased considerably. The inhabitants of the area manufactured arms, shields, jewellery, dishes, and statues. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Age">Iron Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Iron Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hallstatt_Period">Hallstatt Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hallstatt Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The arrival of tribes from <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> disrupted the people of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalenderberg_culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kalenderberg culture (page does not exist)">Kalenderberg culture</a>, who lived in the hamlets located on the plain (<a href="/wiki/Sere%C4%8F" title="SereÄ">SereÄ</a>) and in the hill forts like MolpÃ­r, near <a href="/wiki/Smolenice" title="Smolenice">Smolenice</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Little_Carpathians" title="Little Carpathians">Little Carpathians</a>. During Hallstatt times, monumental burial mounds were erected in western Slovakia, with princely equipment consisting of richly decorated vessels, ornaments and decorations. The burial rites consisted entirely of cremation. Common people were buried in flat urnfield cemeteries. </p>
      <p>A special role was given to weaving and the production of textiles. The local power of the "Princes" of the <a href="/wiki/Hallstatt_culture" title="Hallstatt culture">Hallstatt period</a> disappeared in Slovakia during the century before the middle of first millennium BC, after strife between the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scytho</a>-Thracian people and locals, resulting in abandonment of the old hill-forts. Relatively depopulated areas soon caught the interest of emerging <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> tribes, who advanced from the south towards the north, following the Slovak rivers, peacefully integrating into the remnants of the local population. </p> 
      <h4><span id="La_T.C3.A8ne_Period"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="La_TÃ¨ne_Period">La TÃ¨ne Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: La TÃ¨ne Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>From around 500&nbsp;BCE, the territory of modern-day Slovakia was settled by <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celts</a>, who built powerful <i><a href="/wiki/Oppida" class="mw-redirect" title="Oppida">oppida</a></i> on the sites of modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn" title="DevÃ­n">DevÃ­n</a>. <a href="/wiki/Biatec" title="Biatec">Biatecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_coin" title="Silver coin">silver coins</a> with inscriptions in the Latin alphabet, represent the first known use of writing in Slovakia. At the northern regions, remnants of the local population of Lusatian origin, together with Celtic and later Dacian influence, gave rise to the unique <a href="/wiki/P%C3%BAchov_culture" title="PÃºchov culture">PÃºchov culture</a>, with advanced crafts and iron-working, many hill-forts and fortified settlements of central type with the coinage of the "Velkobysterecky" type (no inscriptions, with a horse on one side and ahead on the other). This culture is often connected with the Celtic tribe mentioned in Roman sources as <a href="/wiki/Cotini" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotini">Cotini</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Period">Roman Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Roman Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trencin-Roman2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/220px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/330px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/440px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trencin-Roman2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Roman inscription at the castle hill of <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="TrenÄÃ­n">TrenÄÃ­n</a> (178â179 AD)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 2&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>, the expanding <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> established and maintained a series of outposts around and just south of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, the largest of which were known as <a href="/wiki/Carnuntum" title="Carnuntum">Carnuntum</a> (whose remains are on the main road halfway between Vienna and Bratislava) and <a href="/wiki/Brigetio" class="mw-redirect" title="Brigetio">Brigetio</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Sz%C5%91ny" title="SzÅny">SzÅny</a> at the Slovak-Hungarian border). Such Roman border settlements were built on the present area of <a href="/wiki/Rusovce" title="Rusovce">Rusovce</a>, currently a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>. The military fort was surrounded by a civilian <a href="/wiki/Vicus" title="Vicus">vicus</a> and several farms of the <a href="/wiki/Villa_rustica" title="Villa rustica">villa rustica</a> type. The name of this settlement was <a href="/wiki/Gerulata" title="Gerulata">Gerulata</a>. The military fort had an auxiliary cavalry unit, approximately 300 horses strong, modelled after the <a href="/wiki/Cananefates" title="Cananefates">Cananefates</a>. The remains of Roman buildings have also survived in <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="DevÃ­n Castle">DevÃ­n Castle</a> (present-day downtown Bratislava), the suburbs of DÃºbravka and Stupava, and Bratislava Castle Hill. </p>
      <p>Near the northernmost line of the Roman hinterlands, the <a href="/wiki/Limes_Romanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Limes Romanus">Limes Romanus</a>, there existed the winter camp of <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="TrenÄÃ­n">Laugaricio</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="TrenÄÃ­n">TrenÄÃ­n</a>) where the Auxiliary of Legion&nbsp;II fought and prevailed in a decisive battle over the Germanic <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a> tribe in 179&nbsp;CE during the <a href="/wiki/Marcomannic_Wars" title="Marcomannic Wars">Marcomannic Wars</a>. The Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Vannius" title="Vannius">Vannius</a>, a kingdom founded by the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> tribes of <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a>, as well as several small Germanic and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Celtic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Celtic tribes">Celtic tribes</a>, including the Osi and <a href="/wiki/Cotini" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotini">Cotini</a>, existed in western and central Slovakia from 8â6&nbsp;BCE to 179&nbsp;CE. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_invasions_from_the_4th_to_7th_centuries">Great invasions from the 4th to 7th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Great invasions from the 4th to 7th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the 2nd and 3rd centuries AD, the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> began to leave the Central Asian steppes. They crossed the Danube in 377&nbsp;AD and occupied <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>, which they used for 75&nbsp;years as their base for launching looting-raids into Western Europe. However, Attila's death in 453 brought about the disappearance of the Hun tribe. In 568, a Turko-Mongol tribal confederacy, the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>, conducted its invasion into the Middle Danube region. The Avars occupied the lowlands of the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a> and established an empire dominating the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Basin" title="Pannonian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a>. </p>
      <p>In 623, the Slavic population living in the western parts of Pannonia seceded from their empire after a revolution led by <a href="/wiki/Samo" title="Samo">Samo</a>, a Frankish merchant.<sup id="cite_ref-TÃ¶rtÃ©neti_KronolÃ³gia_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TÃ¶rtÃ©neti_KronolÃ³gia-20">[20]</a></sup> After 626, the Avar power started a gradual decline<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> but its reign lasted to 804. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavic_states">Slavic states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Slavic states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> tribes settled in the territory of present-day Slovakia in the 5th century. Western Slovakia was the centre of <a href="/wiki/Samo" title="Samo">Samo</a>'s empire in the 7th century. A Slavic state known as the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">Principality of Nitra</a> arose in the 8th century and its ruler <a href="/wiki/Pribina" title="Pribina">Pribina</a> had the first known Christian church of the territory of present-day Slovakia consecrated by 828. Together with neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, the principality formed the core of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravian</a> Empire from 833. The high point of this Slavonic empire came with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Saints Cyril and Methodius</a> in 863, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">Duke</a> <a href="/wiki/Rastislav_of_Moravia" title="Rastislav of Moravia">Rastislav</a>, and the territorial expansion under <a href="/wiki/King" title="King">King</a> <a href="/wiki/Sv%C3%A4topluk_I" class="mw-redirect" title="SvÃ¤topluk I">SvÃ¤topluk I</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Great_Moravia_.28830.E2.80.93before_907.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Moravia_(830âbefore_907)">Great Moravia (830âbefore 907)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Great Moravia (830âbefore 907)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/150px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/225px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/300px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1071" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A statue of <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Saint Cyril and Saint Methodius</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Å½ilina">Å½ilina</a>. In 863, they introduced Christianity to what is now Slovakia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Great Moravia arose around 830 when <a href="/wiki/Mojmir_I_of_Moravia" title="Mojmir I of Moravia">MojmÃ­r I</a> unified the <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> tribes settled north of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and extended the Moravian supremacy over them.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> When MojmÃ­r I endeavoured to secede from the supremacy of the king of <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a> in 846, King <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_German" title="Louis the German">Louis the German</a> deposed him and assisted MojmÃ­r's nephew <a href="/wiki/Rastislav_of_Moravia" title="Rastislav of Moravia">Rastislav</a> (846â870) in acquiring the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-Korai_Magyar_TÃ¶rtÃ©neti_Lexikon_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Korai_Magyar_TÃ¶rtÃ©neti_Lexikon-23">[23]</a></sup> The new monarch pursued an independent policy: after stopping a Frankish attack in 855, he also sought to weaken the influence of Frankish priests preaching in his realm. Duke Rastislav asked the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_III" title="Michael III">Michael III</a> to send teachers who would interpret Christianity in the Slavic vernacular. </p>
      <p>Upon Rastislav's request, two brothers, Byzantine officials and missionaries <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Saints Cyril and Methodius</a> came in 863. Cyril developed the <a href="/wiki/Glagolitic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Glagolitic alphabet">first Slavic alphabet</a> and translated the Gospel into the <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a> language. Rastislav was also preoccupied with the security and administration of his state. Numerous fortified castles built throughout the country are dated to his reign and some of them (e.g.,&nbsp;<i>Dowina</i>, sometimes identified with <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="DevÃ­n Castle">DevÃ­n Castle</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-worldarcheology_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldarcheology-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-caplovic_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caplovic-25">[25]</a></sup> are also mentioned in connection with Rastislav by Frankish chronicles.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fulda_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fulda-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Letter_svatopluk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The papal letter &quot;Industriae Tuae&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/180px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/270px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/360px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1624" data-file-height="2016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Letter_svatopluk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Scire vos volumus</i>, a letter written in 879 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_VIII" title="Pope John VIII">Pope John VIII</a> to <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Svatopluk I">Svatopluk I</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During Rastislav's reign, the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">Principality of Nitra</a> was given to his nephew <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I_of_Moravia" title="Svatopluk I of Moravia">SvÃ¤topluk</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Appanage" title="Appanage">appanage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-caplovic_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caplovic-25">[25]</a></sup> The rebellious prince allied himself with the Franks and overthrew his uncle in 870. Similarly to his predecessor, SvÃ¤topluk I (871â894) assumed the title of the king (<i>rex</i>). During his reign, the Great Moravian Empire reached its greatest territorial extent, when not only present-day <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> and Slovakia but also present-day northern and <a href="/wiki/Central_Hungary" title="Central Hungary">central Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Austria" title="Lower Austria">Lower Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>, southern Poland and <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">northern Serbia</a> belonged to the empire, but the exact borders of his domains are still disputed by modern authors.<sup id="cite_ref-TÃ³th_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TÃ³th-28">[28]</a></sup> Svatopluk also withstood attacks of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Magyar</a> tribes and the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a>, although sometimes it was he who hired the Magyars when waging war against East Francia.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 880, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_VIII" title="Pope John VIII">Pope John&nbsp;VIII</a> set up an independent <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_province" title="Ecclesiastical province">ecclesiastical province</a> in Great Moravia with Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Methodius</a> as its head. He also named the German cleric <a href="/wiki/Wiching" title="Wiching">Wiching</a> the Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">Nitra</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Great_Moravia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Great_Moravia.svg/220px-Great_Moravia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Great_Moravia.svg/330px-Great_Moravia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Great_Moravia.svg/440px-Great_Moravia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="439"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Great_Moravia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Certain and disputed borders of Great Moravia under <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I_of_Moravia" title="Svatopluk I of Moravia">Svatopluk I</a> (according to modern historians)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the death of Prince Svatopluk in 894, his sons <a href="/wiki/Mojmir_II_of_Moravia" title="Mojmir II of Moravia">MojmÃ­r&nbsp;II</a> (894â906?) and <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_II" title="Svatopluk II">Svatopluk&nbsp;II</a> succeeded him as the Prince of Great Moravia and the Prince of Nitra respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-caplovic_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caplovic-25">[25]</a></sup> However, they started to quarrel for domination of the whole empire. Weakened by an internal conflict as well as by constant warfare with <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Francia" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Francia">Eastern Francia</a>, Great Moravia lost most of its peripheral territories. </p>
      <p>In the meantime, the semi-nomadic Magyar tribes, possibly having suffered defeat from the similarly nomadic <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>, left their territories east of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> invaded the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a> and started to occupy the territory gradually around 896.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Their armies' advance may have been promoted by continuous wars among the countries of the region whose rulers still hired them occasionally to intervene in their struggles.<sup id="cite_ref-KristÃ³_2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KristÃ³_2-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It is not known what happened with both MojmÃ­r&nbsp;II and Svatopluk&nbsp;II because they are not mentioned in written sources after 906. In <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pressburg" title="Battle of Pressburg">three battles</a> (4â5 July and 9 August 907) near <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, the Magyars routed <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> armies. Some historians put this year as the date of the break-up of the Great Moravian Empire, due to the Hungarian conquest; other historians take the date a little bit earlier (to 902). </p>
      <p>Great Moravia left behind a lasting legacy in Central and Eastern Europe. The <a href="/wiki/Glagolitic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Glagolitic alphabet">Glagolitic script</a> and its successor <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a> were disseminated to other Slavic countries, charting a new path in their <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">sociocultural development</a>. The administrative system of <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a> may have influenced the development of the administration of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Kingdom_of_Hungary_.281000.E2.80.931918.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1000â1918)">Kingdom of Hungary (1000â1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Hungary (1000â1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/170px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/255px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/340px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="823" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">Stephen I</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">King of Hungary</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the disintegration of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Moravian Empire">Great Moravian Empire</a> at the turn of the 10th century, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian people">Hungarians</a> annexed the territory comprising modern Slovakia. After their defeat on the <a href="/wiki/Lech_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Lech River">Lech River</a> they abandoned their nomadic ways; they settled in the centre of the Carpathian valley, adopted Christianity and began to build a new stateâthe Hungarian kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From the 11th century, when the territory inhabited by the Slavic-speaking population of Danubian Basin was incorporated into the Kingdom of Hungary, until 1918, when the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian empire">Austro-Hungarian empire</a> collapsed, the territory of modern Slovakia was an integral part of the Hungarian state.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The ethnic composition became more diverse with the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Germans" title="Carpathian Germans">Carpathian Germans</a> in the 13th century, and the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> in the 14th century. </p>
      <p>A significant decline in the population resulted from the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">invasion of the Mongols</a> in 1241 and the subsequent famine. However, in medieval times the area of the present-day Slovakia was characterised by German and <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> immigration, burgeoning towns, construction of numerous stone castles, and the cultivation of the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-tibensky_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tibensky-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1465, King <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthias Corvinus of Hungary">Matthias Corvinus</a> founded the Hungarian Kingdom's third university, in Pressburg (Bratislava, Pozsony), but it was closed in 1490 after his death.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">Hussites</a> also settled in the region after the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1franci2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/170px-1franci2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/255px-1franci2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/340px-1franci2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1062" data-file-height="1334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1franci2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>One of the commanders of a Slovak volunteers' army captain <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Francisci-Rimavsk%C3%BD" title="JÃ¡n Francisci-RimavskÃ½">JÃ¡n Francisci-RimavskÃ½</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Uprising_of_1848%E2%80%9349" title="Slovak Uprising of 1848â49">fight for independence from the Kingdom of Hungary</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Owing to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>'s expansion into Hungarian territory, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> was designated the new capital of Hungary in 1536, ahead of the old Hungarian capital of <a href="/wiki/Buda" title="Buda">Buda</a> falling in 1541. It became part of the Austrian Habsburg monarchy, marking the beginning of a new era. The territory comprising modern Slovakia, then known as <a href="/wiki/Upper_Hungary" title="Upper Hungary">Upper Hungary</a>, became the place of settlement for nearly two-thirds of the <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">Magyar</a> nobility fleeing the Turks and far more linguistically and culturally Hungarian than it was before.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-39">[39]</a></sup> Partly thanks to old <a href="/wiki/Hussite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussite">Hussite</a> families, and Slovaks studying under <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>, the region then experienced a growth in <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-39">[39]</a></sup> For a short period in the 17th century, most Slovaks were <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-39">[39]</a></sup> They defied the Catholic Habsburgs and sought protection from neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, a rival continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">Magyar</a> state that practised religious tolerance and normally had Ottoman backing. Upper Hungary, modern Slovakia, became the site of frequent wars between Catholics in the west territory and Protestants in the east, also against Turks, the frontier was on a constant state of military alert and heavily fortified by castles and citadels often manned by Catholic German and Slovak troops on the Habsburg side. By 1648, Slovakia was not spared the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>, which brought the majority of its population from Lutheranism back to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>. In 1655, the printing press at the <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">Trnava</a> university produced the Jesuit Benedikt SzÃ¶llÅsi's Cantus Catholici, a Catholic hymnal in the Slovak language that reaffirmed links to the earlier works of Cyril and Methodius. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">Ottoman wars</a>, the rivalry between <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, and the frequent insurrections against the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> inflicted a great deal of devastation, especially in the rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_(1663%E2%80%931664)" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Turkish War (1663â1664)">Austro-Turkish War (1663â1664)</a> a Turkish army led by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a> decimated Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-39">[39]</a></sup> Even so, <a href="/wiki/Emeric_Th%C3%B6k%C3%B6ly" title="Emeric ThÃ¶kÃ¶ly">ThÃ¶kÃ¶ly</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kuruc" title="Kuruc">kuruc</a> rebels from the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Upper_Hungary" title="Principality of Upper Hungary">Principality of Upper Hungary</a> fought alongside the Turks against the Austrians and Poles at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Battle of Vienna</a> of 1683 led by <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a>. As the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Turks withdrew</a> from Hungary in the late 17th century, the importance of the territory comprising modern Slovakia decreased, although <a href="/wiki/Pressburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressburg">Pressburg</a> retained its status as the capital of Hungary until 1848 when it was transferred back to Buda.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Habsburg_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Habsburg areas">revolution of 1848â49</a>, the Slovaks supported the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Austria" title="Emperor of Austria">Austrian Emperor</a>, hoping for independence from the Hungarian part of the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Dual Monarchy</a>, but they failed to achieve their aim. Thereafter relations between the nationalities deteriorated (see <a href="/wiki/Magyarization" title="Magyarization">Magyarization</a>), culminating in the secession of Slovakia from Hungary after World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Czechoslovakia_.281918.E2.80.931939.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Czechoslovakia_(1918â1939)">Czechoslovakia (1918â1939)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Czechoslovakia (1918â1939)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/220px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/330px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/440px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A monument to <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" class="mw-redirect" title="TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk">TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Å tefÃ¡nik">Milan Å tefÃ¡nik</a>âboth key figures in early Czechoslovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg/220px-Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg/330px-Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg/440px-Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="486"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prohl%C3%A1%C5%A1en%C3%AD_nez%C3%A1vislosti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_declaration_of_independence" title="Czechoslovak declaration of independence">Czechoslovak declaration of independence</a> by <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" class="mw-redirect" title="TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk">TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk</a> in the United States, 1918.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 18 October 1918, <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" class="mw-redirect" title="TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk">TomÃ¡Å¡ Garrigue Masaryk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Å tefÃ¡nik">Milan Rastislav Å tefÃ¡nik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Bene%C5%A1" title="Edvard BeneÅ¡">Edvard BeneÅ¡</a> declared in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_declaration_of_independence" title="Czechoslovak declaration of independence">independence</a> for the territories of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Moravia" title="Margraviate of Moravia">Moravia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upper_Hungary" title="Upper Hungary">Upper Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Ruthenia" title="Carpathian Ruthenia">Carpathian Ruthenia</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> and proclaimed a common state, <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">Czechoslovakia</a>. In 1919, during the chaos following the break-up of Austria-Hungary, Czechoslovakia was formed with numerous <a href="/wiki/German_people" class="mw-redirect" title="German people">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a> and Ruthenians within the newly set borders. The borders were set by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint-Germain-en-Laye_(1919)" title="Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1919)">Treaty of Saint Germain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>. In the peace following the World War, Czechoslovakia emerged as a sovereign European state. It provided what were at the time rather extensive rights to its minorities, at least on paper. </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, democratic Czechoslovakia was allied with France, and also with <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Little_Entente" title="Little Entente">Little Entente</a>); however, the <a href="/wiki/Locarno_Treaties" title="Locarno Treaties">Locarno Treaties</a> of 1925 left East European security open. Both Czechs and Slovaks enjoyed a period of relative prosperity. There was progress in not only the development of the country's economy but also culture and educational opportunities. Yet the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> caused a sharp economic downturn, followed by political disruption and insecurity in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1930s Czechoslovakia came under continuous pressure from the <a href="/wiki/Revanchism" title="Revanchism">revisionist</a> governments of Germany, Hungary and Poland who used the aggrieved minorities in the country as a useful vehicle. Revision of the borders was called for, as Czechs constituted only 43% of the population. Eventually, this pressure led to the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> of September 1938, which allowed the majority ethnic Germans in the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>, borderlands of Czechoslovakia, to join with Germany. The remaining minorities stepped up their pressures for autonomy and the State became federalised, with Diets in Slovakia and Ruthenia. The remainder of Czechoslovakia was renamed Czecho-Slovakia and promised a greater degree of Slovak political autonomy. This, however, failed to materialize.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Parts of southern and eastern Slovakia were also reclaimed by Hungary at the <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_Award" title="First Vienna Award">First Vienna Award</a> of November 1938. </p> 
      <h3><span id="World_War_II_.281939.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_(1939â1945)">World War II (1939â1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: World War II (1939â1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939â1945)">Slovak Republic (1939â1945)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_during_World_War_II" title="Slovakia during World War II">Slovakia during World War II</a>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
