       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Award" title="Vienna Award">Vienna Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> threatened to annex part of Slovakia and allow the remaining regions to be partitioned by Hungary or Poland unless independence was declared.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Thus, Slovakia seceded from Czecho-Slovakia in March 1939 and allied itself, as demanded by Germany, with <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Hitler's</a> coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Secession had created the first Slovak state in history.<sup id="cite_ref-RadioPrague_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RadioPrague-46">[46]</a></sup> The government of the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939â1945)">First Slovak Republic</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">Jozef Tiso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojtech_Tuka" title="Vojtech Tuka">Vojtech Tuka</a>, was strongly influenced by Germany and gradually became a <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet regime</a> in many respects. </p>
      <p>Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_government-in-exile" title="Czechoslovak government-in-exile">Czechoslovak government-in-exile</a> sought to reverse the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> and the subsequent German occupation of Czechoslovakia and to return the Republic to its 1937 boundaries. The government operated from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and it was ultimately considered, by those countries that recognised it, the legitimate government for Czechoslovakia throughout the Second World War. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/220px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/330px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/440px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2033" data-file-height="1413"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Troops of Slovak anti-Nazi <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">resistance movement</a> in 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Slovakia" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Slovakia">Holocaust in Slovakia</a>, 75,000 Jews out of 80,000 who remained on Slovak territory after Hungary had seized southern regions were deported and taken to German <a href="/wiki/Death_camps" class="mw-redirect" title="Death camps">death camps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Thousands of Jews, Gypsies and other politically undesirable people remained in Slovak forced labor camps in <a href="/wiki/Sere%C4%8F_concentration_camp" title="SereÄ concentration camp">SereÄ</a>, Vyhne, and NovÃ¡ky.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Tiso, through the granting of presidential exceptions, allowed between 1,000 and 4,000 people crucial to the war economy to avoid deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Under Tiso's government and Hungarian occupation, the vast majority of Slovakia's pre-war Jewish population (between 75,000 and 105,000 individuals including those who perished from the occupied territory) were murdered.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The Slovak state paid Germany 500 <a href="/wiki/Reichsmark" title="Reichsmark">RM</a> per every deported Jew for "retraining and accommodation" (a similar but smaller payment of 30 RM was paid by <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Croatia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After it became clear that the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> was going to push the Nazis out of eastern and central Europe, an anti-Nazi <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">resistance movement</a> launched a fierce armed insurrection, known as the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_National_Uprising" title="Slovak National Uprising">Slovak National Uprising</a>, near the end of summer 1944. A bloody German occupation and a guerilla war followed. Germans and their <a href="/wiki/Hlinka_Guard" title="Hlinka Guard">local collaborators</a> completely destroyed 93 villages and massacred thousands of civilians, often hundreds at a time.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The territory of Slovakia was liberated by Soviet and Romanian forces by the end of April 1945. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Soviet_influence_and_Communist_party_rule_.281948.E2.80.931989.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_influence_and_Communist_party_rule_(1948â1989)">Soviet influence and Communist party rule (1948â1989)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Soviet influence and Communist party rule (1948â1989)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:199px;max-width:199px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:197px;max-width:197px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/195px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg" decoding="async" width="195" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/293px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/390px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="649"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           The <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> ended 41 years of authoritarian Communist rule in <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> in 1989.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After World War&nbsp;II, Czechoslovakia was reconstituted and <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">Jozef Tiso</a> was executed in 1947 for collaboration with the Nazis. More than <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia#Population_exchanges" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">80,000 Hungarians</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and 32,000 Germans<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> were forced to leave Slovakia, in a series of <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Germans_after_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Expulsion of Germans after World War II">population transfers</a> initiated by the Allies at the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">Potsdam Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rock_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rock-57">[57]</a></sup> Out of about 130,000 <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Germans" title="Carpathian Germans">Carpathian Germans</a> in Slovakia in 1938, by 1947 only some 20,000 remained.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The NKVD arrested and deported over 20,000 people to Siberia<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>, Czechoslovakia came under the influence and later under direct occupation of the Soviet Union and its <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, after a <a href="/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1948 Czechoslovak coup d'Ã©tat">coup in 1948</a>. Eight thousand two hundred and forty people went to forced labour camps in 1948â1953.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1968, following the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a>, the country was <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">invaded</a> by the Warsaw Pact forces (<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People's Republic of Bulgaria">People's Republic of Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic" title="Hungarian People's Republic">People's Republic of Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic" title="Polish People's Republic">People's Republic of Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Socialist Republic of Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People's Socialist Republic of Albania">People's Socialist Republic of Albania</a>) in 1968, ending a <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">period of liberalisation</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dub%C4%8Dek" title="Alexander DubÄek">Alexander DubÄek</a>. 137 Czechoslovak civilians were killed<sup id="cite_ref-victims_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-victims-61">[61]</a></sup> and 500 seriously wounded during the occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-victims2_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-victims2-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1969 Czechoslovakia became a federation of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Socialist Republic">Czech Socialist Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak Socialist Republic">Slovak Socialist Republic</a>. Czechoslovakia became a <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of the Soviet Union. <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovak Socialist Republic</a> was never part of the Soviet Union and remained independent to a degree. </p>
      <p>Borders with the West were protected by the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>. About 600 people, men, women, and children, were killed on the Czechoslovak border with <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> between 1948 and 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Slovak_Republic_.281993.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovak_Republic_(1993âpresent)">Slovak Republic (1993âpresent)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Slovak Republic (1993âpresent)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Slovakia became a member of the European Union in 2004 and signed the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> in 2007.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The end of Communist rule in Czechoslovakia in 1989, during the peaceful <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a>, was followed once again by the country's dissolution, this time into two <a href="/wiki/Succession_of_states" title="Succession of states">successor states</a>. The word "socialist" was dropped in the names of the two republics, with the Slovak Socialist Republic renamed as Slovak Republic. On 17 July 1992, Slovakia, led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_Me%C4%8Diar" title="VladimÃ­r MeÄiar">VladimÃ­r MeÄiar</a>, declared itself a sovereign state, meaning that its laws took precedence over those of the federal government. Throughout the autumn of 1992, MeÄiar and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of the Czech Republic">Czech Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Klaus" title="VÃ¡clav Klaus">VÃ¡clav Klaus</a> negotiated the details for disbanding the federation. In November, the federal parliament voted to dissolve the country officially on 31 December 1992. </p>
      <p>The Slovak Republic and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> went their separate ways after 1 January 1993, an event sometimes called the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">Velvet Divorce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Slovakia has, nevertheless, remained a close partner with the Czech Republic. Both countries co-operate with Hungary and Poland in the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="VisegrÃ¡d Group">VisegrÃ¡d Group</a>. Slovakia became a member of NATO on 29 March 2004 and of the European Union on 1 May 2004. On 1 January 2009, Slovakia adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> as its national currency.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Zuzana_%C4%8Caputov%C3%A1" title="Zuzana ÄaputovÃ¡">Zuzana ÄaputovÃ¡</a> became Slovakia's first female president.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Slovakia" title="Geography of Slovakia">Geography of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Geomorphological_division_of_Slovakia" title="Geomorphological division of Slovakia">Geomorphological division of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of the High Tatras"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg/1000px-High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg/1500px-High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg/2000px-High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7511" data-file-height="1000"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg" title="File:High Tatras Panorama.jpg"> </a>
         </div>Panorama of the <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">High Tatras</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/47th_parallel_north" title="47th parallel north">47Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_north" title="50th parallel north">50Â° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/16th_meridian_east" title="16th meridian east">16Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/23rd_meridian_east" title="23rd meridian east">23Â° E</a>. The Slovak landscape is noted primarily for its mountainous nature, with the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> extending across most of the northern half of the country. Among these <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a> are the high peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Fatra-Tatra_Area" title="Fatra-Tatra Area">Fatra-Tatra Area</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ve%C4%BEk%C3%A1_Fatra" title="VeÄ¾kÃ¡ Fatra">Greater Fatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Fatra" class="mw-redirect" title="Lesser Fatra">Lesser Fatra</a>), <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Ore_Mountains" title="Slovak Ore Mountains">Slovak Ore Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Central_Mountains" title="Slovak Central Mountains">Slovak Central Mountains</a> or <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">Beskids</a>. The largest lowland is the fertile <a href="/wiki/Danubian_Lowland" title="Danubian Lowland">Danubian Lowland</a> in the southwest, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Slovak_Lowland" title="Eastern Slovak Lowland">Eastern Slovak Lowland</a> in the southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-68">[68]</a></sup> Forests cover 41% of Slovak land surface.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tatra_mountains">Tatra mountains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tatra mountains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Slovakia_topo.jpg/300px-Slovakia_topo.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Slovakia_topo.jpg/450px-Slovakia_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Slovakia_topo.jpg/600px-Slovakia_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="962"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topographical</a> map of Slovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Tatra Mountains, with 29 peaks higher than 2,500 metres (8,202 feet) <a href="/wiki/Sea_level#AMSL" title="Sea level">AMSL</a>, are the highest mountain range in the Carpathian Mountains. The Tatras occupy an area of 750 square kilometres (290&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), of which the greater part 600 square kilometres (232&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) lies in Slovakia. They are divided into several parts. </p>
      <p>To the north, close to the Polish border, are the <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">High Tatras</a> which are a popular <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> destination and home to many scenic lakes and valleys as well as the highest point in Slovakia, the <a href="/wiki/Gerlachovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt" title="GerlachovskÃ½ Å¡tÃ­t">GerlachovskÃ½ Å¡tÃ­t</a> at 2,655 metres (8,711&nbsp;ft) and the country's highly symbolic mountain <a href="/wiki/Kriv%C3%A1%C5%88_(peak)" title="KrivÃ¡Å (peak)">KrivÃ¡Å</a>. To the west are the <a href="/wiki/Western_Tatras" title="Western Tatras">Western Tatras</a> with their highest peak of <a href="/wiki/Bystr%C3%A1_(mountain)" title="BystrÃ¡ (mountain)">BystrÃ¡</a> at 2,248 metres (7,375&nbsp;ft) and to the east are the <a href="/wiki/Belianske_Tatras" title="Belianske Tatras">Belianske Tatras</a>, smallest by area. </p>
      <p>Separated from the Tatras proper by the valley of the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="VÃ¡h">VÃ¡h</a> river are the <a href="/wiki/Low_Tatras" title="Low Tatras">Low Tatras</a>, with their highest peak of <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Eumbier" title="Äumbier">Äumbier</a> at 2,043 metres (6,703&nbsp;ft). </p>
      <p>The Tatra mountain range is represented as one of the three hills on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Slovakia" title="Coat of arms of Slovakia">coat of arms of Slovakia</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Slovakia" title="List of national parks of Slovakia">List of national parks of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG/220px-Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG/330px-Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG/440px-Palcmansk%C3%A1_Ma%C5%A1a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caves">Caves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Caves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_caves_in_Slovakia" title="List of caves in Slovakia">List of caves in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Domica_Cave_20.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Domica_Cave_20.jpg/220px-Domica_Cave_20.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Domica_Cave_20.jpg/330px-Domica_Cave_20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Domica_Cave_20.jpg/440px-Domica_Cave_20.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Domica_Cave_20.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Domica" class="mw-redirect" title="Domica">Domica</a> Cave
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia has hundreds of caves and caverns under its mountains, of which 30 are open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Most of the caves have <a href="/wiki/Stalagmite" title="Stalagmite">stalagmites</a> rising from the ground and <a href="/wiki/Stalactite" title="Stalactite">stalactites</a> hanging from above. There are currently five Slovak caves under <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s World Heritage Site status. They are <a href="/wiki/Dob%C5%A1in%C3%A1_Ice_Cave" title="DobÅ¡inÃ¡ Ice Cave">DobÅ¡inÃ¡ Ice Cave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domica" class="mw-redirect" title="Domica">Domica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gombasek_Cave" title="Gombasek Cave">Gombasek Cave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasovsk%C3%A1_Cave" title="JasovskÃ¡ Cave">JasovskÃ¡ Cave</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ochtinsk%C3%A1_Aragonite_Cave" title="OchtinskÃ¡ Aragonite Cave">OchtinskÃ¡ Aragonite Cave</a>. Other caves open to the public include <a href="/wiki/Belianska_Cave" title="Belianska Cave">Belianska Cave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dem%C3%A4novsk%C3%A1_Cave_of_Liberty" title="DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ Cave of Liberty">DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ Cave of Liberty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dem%C3%A4novsk%C3%A1_Ice_Cave" title="DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ Ice Cave">DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ Ice Cave</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bystrianska_Cave" title="Bystrianska Cave">Bystrianska Cave</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">Rivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rivers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Slovakia" title="List of rivers of Slovakia">List of rivers of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bel%C3%A1_river_(Slovakia).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg/220px-Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg/330px-Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg/440px-Bel%C3%A1_river_%28Slovakia%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="530"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bel%C3%A1_river_(Slovakia).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A1_(river)" title="BelÃ¡ (river)">BelÃ¡ River</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of the rivers arise in the Slovak mountains. Some only pass through Slovakia, while others make a natural border with surrounding countries (more than 620 kilometres [390&nbsp;mi]). For example, the <a href="/wiki/Dunajec" title="Dunajec">Dunajec</a> (17 kilometres [11&nbsp;mi]) to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Danube_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Danube River">Danube</a> (172 kilometres [107&nbsp;mi]) to the south or the <a href="/wiki/Morava_(river)" title="Morava (river)">Morava</a> (119 kilometres [74&nbsp;mi]) to the West. The total length of the rivers on Slovak territory is 49,774 kilometres (30,928&nbsp;mi). </p>
      <p>The longest river in Slovakia is the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="VÃ¡h">VÃ¡h</a> (403 kilometres [250&nbsp;mi]), the shortest is the Äierna voda. Other important and large rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Myjava_(river)" title="Myjava (river)">Myjava</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nitra_(river)" title="Nitra (river)">Nitra</a> (197 kilometres [122&nbsp;mi]), the <a href="/wiki/Orava_(river)" title="Orava (river)">Orava</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hron" title="Hron">Hron</a> (298 kilometres [185&nbsp;mi]), the <a href="/wiki/Horn%C3%A1d" title="HornÃ¡d">HornÃ¡d</a> (193 kilometres [120&nbsp;mi]), the <a href="/wiki/Slan%C3%A1_river" class="mw-redirect" title="SlanÃ¡ river">SlanÃ¡</a> (110 kilometres [68&nbsp;mi]), the <a href="/wiki/Ipe%C4%BE" title="IpeÄ¾">IpeÄ¾</a> (232 kilometres [144&nbsp;mi], forming the border with Hungary), the <a href="/wiki/Bodrog" title="Bodrog">Bodrog</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Laborec" title="Laborec">Laborec</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latorica" title="Latorica">Latorica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ondava" title="Ondava">Ondava</a>. </p>
      <p>The biggest volume of discharge in Slovak rivers is during <a href="/wiki/Spring_(season)" title="Spring (season)">spring</a>, when the snow melts from the mountains. The only exception is the Danube, whose discharge is the greatest during summer when the snow melts in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>. The Danube is the largest river that flows through Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1769" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SVK_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> types of Slovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Slovak climate lies between the temperate and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> zones with relatively warm <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summers</a> and cold, cloudy and humid <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winters</a>. Temperature extremes are between â41 to 40.3&nbsp;Â°C (â41.8 to 104.5&nbsp;Â°F) although temperatures below â30&nbsp;Â°C (â22&nbsp;Â°F) are rare. The weather differs from the mountainous north to the plains in the south. </p>
      <p>The warmest region is <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and Southern Slovakia where the temperatures may reach 30&nbsp;Â°C (86&nbsp;Â°F) in summer, occasionally to 39&nbsp;Â°C (102&nbsp;Â°F) in <a href="/wiki/Hurbanovo" title="Hurbanovo">Hurbanovo</a>. During night, the temperatures drop to 20&nbsp;Â°C (68&nbsp;Â°F). The daily temperatures in winter average in the range of â5&nbsp;Â°C (23&nbsp;Â°F) to 10&nbsp;Â°C (50&nbsp;Â°F). During night it may be freezing, but usually not below â10&nbsp;Â°C (14&nbsp;Â°F). </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:199px;max-width:199px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG/190px-CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG" decoding="async" width="190" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG/285px-CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG/380px-CulHer14Slovakia328.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2488" data-file-height="1909"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Summer in <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1sk%C3%A9_Podhradie" title="SpiÅ¡skÃ© Podhradie">SpiÅ¡skÃ© Podhradie</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:197px;max-width:197px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG/195px-Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG" decoding="async" width="195" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG/293px-Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG/390px-Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica_im_Herbst.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Winter in <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica" title="BanskÃ¡ Å tiavnica">BanskÃ¡ Å tiavnica</a>; the town is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Slovakia, there are four <a href="/wiki/Season" title="Season">seasons</a>, each season (<a href="/wiki/Spring_(season)" title="Spring (season)">spring</a>, summer, <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">autumn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a>) lasts three months. The dry continental air brings in the summer heat and winter frosts. In contrast, oceanic air brings rainfalls and reduces summer temperatures. In the lowlands and valleys, there is often fog, especially in winter. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png/220px-Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png/330px-Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png/440px-Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="409"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Hardiness_Zones.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hardiness zones of Slovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Spring starts with 21 March and is characterised by colder weather with an average daily temperature of 9&nbsp;Â°C (48&nbsp;Â°F) in the first weeks and about 14&nbsp;Â°C (57&nbsp;Â°F) in May and 17&nbsp;Â°C (63&nbsp;Â°F) in June. In Slovakia, the weather and climate in the spring are very unstable. </p>
      <p>Summer starts on 22 June and is usually characterised by hot weather with daily temperatures exceeding 30&nbsp;Â°C (86&nbsp;Â°F). July is the warmest month with temperatures up to about 37 to 40&nbsp;Â°C (99 to 104&nbsp;Â°F), especially in regions of southern Slovakiaâin the urban area of KomÃ¡rno, Hurbanovo or Å tÃºrovo. Showers or thunderstorms may occur because of the summer monsoon called Medardova kvapka (Medard dropâ40 days of rain). Summer in Northern Slovakia is usually mild with temperatures around 25&nbsp;Â°C (77&nbsp;Â°F) (less in the mountains). </p>
      <p>Autumn in Slovakia starts on 23 September and is mostly characterised by wet weather and wind, although the first weeks can be very warm and sunny. The average temperature in September is around 14&nbsp;Â°C (57&nbsp;Â°F), in November to 3&nbsp;Â°C (37&nbsp;Â°F). Late September and early October is a dry and sunny time of year (so-called <a href="/wiki/Indian_summer" title="Indian summer">Indian summer</a>). </p>
      <p>Winter starts on 21 December with temperatures around â5 to â10&nbsp;Â°C (23 to 14&nbsp;Â°F). In December and January, it is usually snowing, these are the coldest months of the year. At lower altitudes, snow does not stay the whole winter, it changes into the thaw and frost. Winters are colder in the mountains, where the snow usually lasts until March or April and the night temperatures fall to â20&nbsp;Â°C (â4&nbsp;Â°F) and colder.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Endemic_Plant_Species_in_Slovakia" title="Endemic Plant Species in Slovakia">Endemic Plant Species in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry,_Dolina_Bielej_vody,_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_(32).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG/220px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG/330px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG/440px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Dolina_Bielej_vody%2C_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_%2832%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3119" data-file-height="2481"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry,_Dolina_Bielej_vody,_cestou_od_Zelen%C3%A9ho_plesa_na_Jah%C5%88ac%C3%AD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt_(32).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Rupicapra_rupicapra_tatrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Rupicapra rupicapra tatrica">Rupicapra rupicapra tatrica</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 19 May 1993, and became a party to the convention on 25 August 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan" title="Biodiversity action plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, which was received by the convention on 2 November 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The biodiversity of Slovakia comprises <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> (such as annelids, arthropods, molluscs, nematodes and vertebrates), <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ascomycota" title="Ascomycota">Ascomycota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basidiomycota" title="Basidiomycota">Basidiomycota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycota" title="Chytridiomycota">Chytridiomycota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glomeromycota" title="Glomeromycota">Glomeromycota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zygomycota" title="Zygomycota">Zygomycota</a>), micro-organisms (including <a href="/wiki/Mycetozoa" title="Mycetozoa">Mycetozoa</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a>. The geographical position of Slovakia determines the richness of the diversity of fauna and flora. More than 11,000 plant species have been described throughout its territory, nearly 29,000 animal species and over 1,000 species of protozoa. <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">Endemic</a> biodiversity is also common.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia is located in the biome of <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest">temperate broadleaf and mixed forests</a> and terrestrial ecoregions of <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_mixed_forests" title="Pannonian mixed forests">Pannonian mixed forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_montane_conifer_forests" title="Carpathian montane conifer forests">Carpathian montane conifer forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-77">[77]</a></sup> As the altitude changes, the vegetation associations and animal communities are forming height levels (<a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">spruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scrub_pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Scrub pine">scrub pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpine_meadows" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine meadows">alpine meadows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subsoil" title="Subsoil">subsoil</a>). Forests cover 44% of the territory of Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.34/10, ranking it 129th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-79">[79]</a></sup> In terms of forest stands, 60% are <a href="/wiki/Broadleaf_trees" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadleaf trees">broadleaf trees</a> and 40% are <a href="/wiki/Coniferous_trees" class="mw-redirect" title="Coniferous trees">coniferous trees</a>. The occurrence of animal species is strongly connected to the appropriate types of plant associations and biotopes.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Over 4,000 species of fungi have been recorded from Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Of these, nearly 1,500 are <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a>-forming species.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Some of these fungi are undoubtedly endemic, but not enough is known to say how many. Of the lichen-forming species, about 40% have been classified as threatened in some way. About 7% are apparently extinct, 9% endangered, 17% vulnerable, and 7% rare. The conservation status of non-lichen-forming fungi in Slovakia is not well documented, but there is a red list for its larger fungi.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Slovakia" title="Politics of Slovakia">Politics of Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Slovakia" title="Law of Slovakia">Law of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Slovakia" title="Prime Minister of Slovakia">Prime Minister of Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Slovakia" title="President of Slovakia">President of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">

        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">

          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democratic</a> republic with a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The last <a href="/wiki/2020_Slovak_parliamentary_election" title="2020 Slovak parliamentary election">parliamentary elections</a> were held on 29 February 2020 and two rounds of <a href="/wiki/2019_Slovak_presidential_election" title="2019 Slovak presidential election">presidential elections</a> took place on 16 and 30 March 2019. </p>
      <p>The Slovak <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the formal head of the executive is the president (currently <a href="/wiki/Zuzana_%C4%8Caputov%C3%A1" title="Zuzana ÄaputovÃ¡">Zuzana ÄaputovÃ¡</a>, the first female president), though with very limited powers. The president is elected by direct, popular vote under the <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">two-round system</a> for a five-year term. Most <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> power lies with the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, the prime minister (currently <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Heger" title="Eduard Heger">Eduard Heger</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> who is usually the leader of the winning party and who needs to form a majority coalition in the parliament. The prime minister is appointed by the president. The remainder of the cabinet is appointed by the president on the recommendation of the prime minister. </p>
      <p>Slovakia's highest <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a> body is the 150-seat <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Council_(Slovakia)" title="National Council (Slovakia)">National Council of the Slovak Republic</a> (<i>NÃ¡rodnÃ¡ rada Slovenskej republiky</i>). Delegates are elected for a four-year term on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>. </p>
      <p>Slovakia's highest <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial body</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Slovakia" title="Constitutional Court of Slovakia">Constitutional Court of Slovakia</a> (<i>ÃstavnÃ½ sÃºd</i>), which rules on constitutional issues. The 13&nbsp;members of this court are appointed by the president from a slate of candidates nominated by parliament. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Slovakia" title="Constitution of Slovakia">Constitution of the Slovak Republic</a> was ratified 1 September 1992, and became effective 1 January 1993. It was amended in September 1998 to allow <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">direct election</a> of the president and again in February 2001 due to EU admission requirements. The <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law system</a> is based on Austro-Hungarian codes. The <a href="/wiki/Code_of_law" title="Code of law">legal code</a> was modified to comply with the obligations of <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization on Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE) and to expunge the <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="MarxismâLeninism">MarxistâLeninist</a> <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">legal theory</a>. Slovakia accepts the compulsory <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> jurisdiction with reservations. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Slovakia" title="Foreign relations of Slovakia">Foreign relations of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Slovakia" title="List of diplomatic missions of Slovakia">List of diplomatic missions of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_(33889395928).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg/220px-President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg/330px-President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg/440px-President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_%2833889395928%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Trump_Welcomes_the_Prime_Minister_of_the_Slovak_Republic_to_the_White_House_(33889395928).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former Slovak Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pellegrini" title="Peter Pellegrini">Peter Pellegrini</a> with former U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> in the White House, 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Slovakia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Slovakia)">Ministry of Foreign and European Affairs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i lang="sk">Ministerstvo zahraniÄnÃ½ch vecÃ­ a eurÃ³pskych zÃ¡leÅ¾itostÃ­</i>) is responsible for maintaining the Slovak Republic's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Slovakia" title="Foreign relations of Slovakia">external relations</a> and the management of its <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Slovakia" title="List of diplomatic missions of Slovakia">international diplomatic missions</a>. The ministry's <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Slovakia)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Slovakia)">director</a> is <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Kor%C4%8Dok" title="Ivan KorÄok">Ivan KorÄok</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LajcakBio_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LajcakBio-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USDOS_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDOS-87">[87]</a></sup> The ministry oversees Slovakia's affairs with foreign entities, including bilateral relations with individual nations and its representation in international organizations. </p>
      <p>Slovakia joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 2004 and the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> in 2009. </p>
      <p>Slovakia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (since 1993) and participates in its specialized agencies. The country was, on 10 October 2005, elected to a two-year term on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> from 2006 to 2007. It is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (CoE), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a> (UfM), the <a href="/wiki/European_Organization_for_Nuclear_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="European Organization for Nuclear Research">European Organization for Nuclear Research</a> (CERN) and part of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="VisegrÃ¡d Group">VisegrÃ¡d Group</a> (V4: Slovakia, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>). </p>
      <p>In 2020, Slovak citizens had visa-free or visa-on-arrival access to 181 countries and territories, ranking the Slovak passport 11th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava,_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG/220px-Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG/330px-Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG/440px-Bratislava%2C_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2551" data-file-height="1701"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava,_the_Japanese_Embassy.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Embassy of <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia maintains <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic relations</a> with 134 countries, primarily through its <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Slovakia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Slovakia)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>. As of December 2013, Slovakia maintained 90 missions abroad, including 64 embassies, seven missions to multilateral organisations, nine consulates-general, one consular office, one Slovak Economic and Cultural Office and eight Slovak Institutes.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> There are 44 embassies and 35 honorary consulates in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>. </p>
      <p>Slovakia and the United States retain strong <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic ties</a> and cooperate in the <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">military</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency" title="Law enforcement agency">law enforcement</a> areas. The U.S. Department of Defense programs has contributed significantly to Slovak military reforms. Hundreds of thousands of Americans have their roots in Slovakia, and many retain strong cultural and familial ties to the Slovak Republic. President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> and the United States played a major role in the establishment of the original Czechoslovak state on 28 October 1918. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Armed Forces of the Slovak Republic number 14,000 uniformed personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Slovakia joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in March 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The country has been an active participant in US- and NATO-led military actions. There is a joint Czech-Slovak peacekeeping force in Kosovo. From 2006 the army transformed into a fully professional organisation and compulsory military service was abolished. </p>
      <p>Slovak <a href="/wiki/Ground_Forces_of_the_Slovak_Republic" title="Ground Forces of the Slovak Republic">Ground Forces</a> are made up of two active <a href="/wiki/Mechanized_infantry" title="Mechanized infantry">mechanised infantry</a> <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">brigades</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Air_Force" title="Slovak Air Force">Air and Air Defence Forces</a> comprise one <a href="/wiki/Wing_(military_unit)" title="Wing (military unit)">wing</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighters</a>, one wing of utility <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopters</a>, and one SAM brigade. Training and support forces comprise a National Support Element (Multifunctional Battalion, Transport Battalion, Repair Battalion), a garrison force of the capital city Bratislava, as well as a training battalion, and various logistics and communication and information bases. Miscellaneous forces under the direct command of the <a href="/wiki/Staff_(military)" title="Staff (military)">General Staff</a> include the <a href="/wiki/5th_Special_Operations_Regiment_(Slovakia)" title="5th Special Operations Regiment (Slovakia)">5th Special Forces Regiment</a>. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">The US State Department</a> in 2017 reported: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>The government generally respected the human rights of its citizens; however, there were problems in some areas. The most significant human rights issues included incidents of interference with privacy; corruption; widespread discrimination against Roma minority; and security force violence against ethnic and racial minorities government actions and rhetoric did little to discourage. The government investigated reports of abuses by members of the security forces and other government institutions, although some observers questioned the thoroughness of these investigations. Some officials engaged in corrupt practices with impunity. Two former ministers were convicted of corruption during the year.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>Human rights in Slovakia are guaranteed by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Slovakia" title="Constitution of Slovakia">Constitution of Slovakia</a> from the year 1992 and by multiple international laws signed in Slovakia between 1948 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/European_Roma_Rights_Centre" title="European Roma Rights Centre">European Roma Rights Centre</a> (ERRC), <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Slovakia" title="Romani people in Slovakia">Romani people in Slovakia</a> "endure racism in the job market, housing and education fields and are often subjected to forced evictions, vigilante intimidation, disproportionate levels of police brutality and more subtle forms of discrimination."<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Slovakia" title="Regions of Slovakia">Regions of Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Slovakia" title="Districts of Slovakia">Districts of Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_and_towns_in_Slovakia" title="List of municipalities and towns in Slovakia">List of municipalities and towns in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_(35096533142).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg/220px-Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg/330px-Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg/440px-Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_%2835096533142%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4719" data-file-height="3248"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hlavn%C3%A9_Namestie_(35096533142).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, capital and largest city of Slovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia is divided into 8 <i><a href="/wiki/Kraj" title="Kraj">kraje</a></i> (singularâ<i>kraj</i>, usually translated as "region"), each of which is named after its principal city. Regions have enjoyed a certain degree of autonomy since 2002. Their <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-governing</a> bodies are referred to as Self-governing (or autonomous) Regions (sg. <i>samosprÃ¡vny kraj</i>, pl. <i>samosprÃ¡vne kraje</i>) or Upper-Tier Territorial Units (sg. <i>vyÅ¡Å¡Ã­ ÃºzemnÃ½ celok</i>, pl. <i>vyÅ¡Å¡ie ÃºzemnÃ© celky</i>, abbr. VÃC). </p>
      <p>The <i>kraje</i> are subdivided into many <i><a href="/wiki/Okres" title="Okres">okresy</a></i> (sg. <i>okres</i>, usually translated as districts). Slovakia currently has 79&nbsp;districts. </p>
      <p>The <i>okresy</i> are further divided into <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_and_towns_in_Slovakia" title="List of municipalities and towns in Slovakia">obce</a></i> (sg. <i>obec</i>, usually translated as "municipality"). There are currently 2,890 municipalities. </p>
      <p>In terms of economics and <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rate, the western regions are richer than eastern regions. Bratislava is the third-richest region of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> by GDP (PPP) per capita (after <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>); GDP at purchasing power parity is about three times higher than in other Slovak regions.<sup id="cite_ref-finweb.hnonline.sk_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finweb.hnonline.sk-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>

             <td><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Arms of PreÅ¡ov.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg/17px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg.png" decoding="async" width="17" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg/26px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg/34px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pre%C5%A1ov.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="580"></a> <a href="/wiki/Pre%C5%A1ov" title="PreÅ¡ov">PreÅ¡ov</a></td>

             <td><a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice_Region" title="KoÅ¡ice Region">KoÅ¡ice Region</a></td>
