      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Slovakia" title="Economy of Slovakia">Economy of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg/170px-Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg/255px-Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg/340px-Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_Central_Bank3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Slovakia" title="National Bank of Slovakia">National Bank of Slovakia</a> in Bratislava
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Slovak economy is a developed, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> economy, with the GDP per capita equalling 78% of the average of the European Union in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-rich_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rich-98">[98]</a></sup> The country has difficulties addressing regional imbalances in wealth and employment.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> GDP per capita ranges from 188% of EU average in Bratislava to 54% in Eastern Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Although regional income inequality is high, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_home_ownership_rate" title="List of countries by home ownership rate">90% of citizens own their homes</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> in 2017 reported: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>The Slovak Republic continues exhibiting robust economic performance, with strong growth backed by a sound financial sector, low public debt and high international competitiveness drawing on large inward investment.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>In 2020, Slovakia was ranked by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> as the 38th <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">richest country in the world</a> (out of 187 countries), with purchasing power parity per capita GDP of $38,321. The country used to be dubbed the "<a href="/wiki/Tatra_Tiger" title="Tatra Tiger">Tatra Tiger</a>". Slovakia successfully transformed from a centrally <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> to a market-driven economy. Major <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisations</a> are completed, the banking sector is almost completely in private hands, and foreign investment has risen. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/170px-Eurozone.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/255px-Eurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/340px-Eurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Slovakia is part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, the EU single market, and since 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> (dark blue)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Slovak economy is one of the fastest-growing economies in Europe and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">3rd-fastest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (2017). In 2007, 2008 and 2010 (with <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> growth of 10.5%, 6% and 4%, retrospectively). In 2016, more than 86% of Slovak exports went to <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, and more than 50% of Slovak imports came from other European Union member states.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ratio of government debt to GDP in Slovakia reached 49.4% by the end of 2018, far below the OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unemployment, peaking at 19% at the end of 1999, decreased to 4.9% in 2019, lowest recorded rate in Slovak history.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia adopted the Euro currency on 1 January 2009 as the 16th member of the Eurozone. The euro in Slovakia was approved by <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">the European commission</a> on 7 May 2008. The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_koruna" title="Slovak koruna">Slovak koruna</a> was revalued on 28 May 2008 to 30.126 for 1 euro,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> which was also the exchange rate for the euro.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/220px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/330px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/440px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High-rise buildings in Bratislava's business districts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Slovak government encourages foreign investment since it is one of the driving forces of the economy. Slovakia is an attractive country for <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">foreign investors</a> mainly because of its low wages, low tax rates, well educated <a href="/wiki/Labor_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor force">labour force</a>, favourable geographic location in the heart of Central Europe, strong political stability and good international relations reinforced by the country's accession to the European Union. Some regions, mostly at the east of Slovakia have failed to attract major investment, which has aggravated regional disparities in many economic and social areas. <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">Foreign direct investment</a> inflow grew more than 600% from 2000 and cumulatively reached an all-time high of $17.3&nbsp;billion in 2006, or around $22,000 per capita by the end of 2008. </p>
      <p>Slovakia ranks 45th out of 190 economies in terms of ease of doing business, according to the <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">2020 World Bank Doing Business Report</a> and 57th out of the 63 countries in terms of competitive economy, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Competitiveness_Yearbook" title="World Competitiveness Yearbook">2020 World Competitiveness Yearbook Report</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Slovakia" title="Automotive industry in Slovakia">Automotive industry in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/220px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/330px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/440px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/ESET" title="ESET">ESET</a> headquarters in Bratislava
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although Slovakia's GDP comes mainly from the tertiary (services) sector, the industrial sector also plays an important role within its economy. The main industry sectors are <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Slovakia" title="Automotive industry in Slovakia">car manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>. Since 2007, Slovakia has been the world's largest producer of cars per capita,<sup id="cite_ref-Kia_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kia-107">[107]</a></sup> with a total of 1,090,000 cars manufactured in the country in 2018 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-automagazin.sk_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-automagazin.sk-108">[108]</a></sup> 275,000 people are employed directly and indirectly by the automotive industry.<sup id="cite_ref-sario.sk_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sario.sk-109">[109]</a></sup> There are currently four automobile assembly plants: <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>'s in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> (models: <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Up" title="Volkswagen Up">Volkswagen Up</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Touareg" title="Volkswagen Touareg">Volkswagen Touareg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">Audi Q7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q8" title="Audi Q8">Audi Q8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Cayenne" title="Porsche Cayenne">Porsche Cayenne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamborghini_Urus" title="Lamborghini Urus">Lamborghini Urus</a>), <a href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" class="mw-redirect" title="PSA Peugeot CitroÃ«n">PSA Peugeot CitroÃ«n</a>'s in <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">Trnava</a> (models: <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_208" title="Peugeot 208">Peugeot 208</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C3_Picasso" title="CitroÃ«n C3 Picasso">CitroÃ«n C3 Picasso</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Kia Motors">Kia Motors</a>' <a href="/wiki/Kia_Design_and_Manufacturing_Facilities#Å½ilina_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Kia Design and Manufacturing Facilities">Å½ilina Plant</a> (models: <a href="/wiki/Kia_Cee%27d" class="mw-redirect" title="Kia Cee'd">Kia Cee'd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kia_Sportage" title="Kia Sportage">Kia Sportage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kia_Venga" title="Kia Venga">Kia Venga</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Land_Rover" title="Jaguar Land Rover">Jaguar Land Rover</a>'s in <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">Nitra</a> (model: <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover_Discovery" title="Land Rover Discovery">Land Rover Discovery</a>). <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Mobis" title="Hyundai Mobis">Hyundai Mobis</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Å½ilina">Å½ilina</a> is the largest suppliers for the automotive industry in Slovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-etrend.sk_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etrend.sk-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From electrical engineering companies, <a href="/wiki/Foxconn" title="Foxconn">Foxconn</a> has a factory at <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">Nitra</a> for <a href="/wiki/LCD_television" title="LCD television">LCD TV</a> manufacturing, <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Samsung Group">Samsung</a> at <a href="/wiki/Galanta" title="Galanta">Galanta</a> for <a href="/wiki/Computer_monitor" title="Computer monitor">computer monitors</a> and television sets manufacturing. <a href="/wiki/Slovnaft" title="Slovnaft">Slovnaft</a> based in Bratislava with 4,000 employees, is an oil refinery with a processing capacity of 5.5 - 6 million tonnes of crude oil, annually. Steel producer <a href="/wiki/U._S._Steel_Ko%C5%A1ice,_s.r.o." title="U. S. Steel KoÅ¡ice, s.r.o.">U. S. Steel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="KoÅ¡ice">KoÅ¡ice</a> is the largest employer in the east of Slovakia with 12,000 employees. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/220px-Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/330px-Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/440px-Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A graphical depiction of Slovakia's product exports in 21 colour-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/ESET" title="ESET">ESET</a> is an IT security company from Bratislava with more than 1,000<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> employees worldwide at present. Their branch offices are in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high-tech</a>-oriented businesses have prospered in Bratislava. Many global companies, including <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenovo" title="Lenovo">Lenovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, <a href="/wiki/SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="SAP AG">SAP</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>, have built <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">outsourcing</a> and service centres here.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Reasons for the influx of <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multi-national corporations</a> include proximity to Western Europe, skilled labour force and the high density of universities and research facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Other large companies and employers with headquarters in Bratislava include <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Telekom" title="Slovak Telekom">Slovak Telekom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_Slovensko" title="Orange Slovensko">Orange Slovensko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovensk%C3%A1_sporite%C4%BE%C5%88a" title="SlovenskÃ¡ sporiteÄ¾Åa">SlovenskÃ¡ sporiteÄ¾Åa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tatra_banka" title="Tatra banka">Tatra banka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doprastav" title="Doprastav">Doprastav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> Slovakia, <a href="/wiki/Henkel" title="Henkel">Henkel</a> Slovensko, <a href="/wiki/Slovensk%C3%BD_plyn%C3%A1rensk%C3%BD_priemysel" title="SlovenskÃ½ plynÃ¡renskÃ½ priemysel">SlovenskÃ½ plynÃ¡renskÃ½ priemysel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> Slovakia, <a href="/wiki/Mondelez_International" title="Mondelez International">Mondelez Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool_Corporation" title="Whirlpool Corporation">Whirlpool Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Insurance_Group" title="Zurich Insurance Group">Zurich Insurance Group</a> Slovakia. </p>
      <p>Bratislava's geographical position in Central Europe has long made Bratislava a crossroads for <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a> traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Various ancient <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amber_Road" title="Amber Road">Amber Road</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> waterway, have crossed territory of present-day Bratislava. Today, Bratislava is the road, railway, waterway and airway hub.<sup id="cite_ref-transport_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transport-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_electricity_production.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Slovakia_electricity_production.svg/220px-Slovakia_electricity_production.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Slovakia_electricity_production.svg/330px-Slovakia_electricity_production.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Slovakia_electricity_production.svg/440px-Slovakia_electricity_production.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_electricity_production.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Slovakia electricity production by source
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/220px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/330px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/440px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nuclear Power Plant <a href="/wiki/Mochovce_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Mochovce Nuclear Power Plant">Mochovce</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2012, Slovakia produced a total of 28,393 <a href="/wiki/GWh" class="mw-redirect" title="GWh">GWh</a> of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> while at the same time consumed 28 786 GWh. The slightly higher level of consumption than the capacity of production (- 393 GWh) meant the country was not self-sufficient in energy sourcing. Slovakia imported electricity mainly from the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (9,961 GWhâ73.6% of total import) and exported mainly to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (10,231 GWhâ78.2% of total export). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">Nuclear energy</a> accounts for 53.8% of total electricity production in Slovakia, followed by 18.1% of <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">thermal power</a> energy, 15.1% by <a href="/wiki/Hydro_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydro power">hydro power</a> energy, 2% by <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar energy</a>, 9.6% by other sources and the rest 1.4% is imported.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The two nuclear power-plants in Slovakia are in <a href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="JaslovskÃ© Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">JaslovskÃ© Bohunice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mochovce_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Mochovce Nuclear Power Plant">Mochovce</a>, each of them containing two operating reactors. Before the accession of Slovakia to the EU in 2004, the government agreed to turn-off the V1 block of <a href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="JaslovskÃ© Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">JaslovskÃ© Bohunice power-plant</a>, built-in 1978. After deactivating the last of the two reactors of the V1 block in 2008, Slovakia stopped being self-dependent in energy production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Currently there is another block (V2) with two active reactors in <a href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="JaslovskÃ© Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">JaslovskÃ© Bohunice</a>. It is scheduled for decommissioning in 2025. Two new reactors are under construction in Mochovce plant. The nuclear power production in Slovakia occasionally draws the attention of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> green-energy activists who organise protests and block the borders between the two countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Slovakia" title="Transport in Slovakia">Transport in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">

      <p>There are four main highways D1 to D4 and eight expressways R1 to R8. Many of them are still under construction. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Motorway_D1_(Slovakia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway D1 (Slovakia)">D1 motorway</a> connects Bratislava to <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">Trnava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">Nitra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="TrenÄÃ­n">TrenÄÃ­n</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Å½ilina">Å½ilina</a> and beyond, while the <a href="/wiki/Motorway_D2_(Slovakia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway D2 (Slovakia)">D2 motorway</a> connects it to <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">Brno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> in the northâsouth direction. A large part of <a href="/wiki/Motorway_D4_(Slovakia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway D4 (Slovakia)">D4&nbsp;motorway</a> (an outer bypass), which should ease the pressure on Bratislava's highway system, is scheduled to open in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nordostautobahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordostautobahn">A6&nbsp;motorway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> connects Slovakia directly to the Austrian motorway system and was opened on 19 November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia has four international airports. Bratislava's <a href="/wiki/M._R._%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="M. R. Å tefÃ¡nik Airport">M.&nbsp;R.&nbsp;Å tefÃ¡nik Airport</a> is the main and largest <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a>. It is located 9 kilometres (5.6 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a>) northeast of the city centre. It serves civil and governmental, scheduled and unscheduled domestic and international flights. The current runways support the landing of all common types of aircraft currently used. The airport has enjoyed rapidly growing passenger traffic in recent years; it served 279,028&nbsp;passengers in 2000 and 2,292,712 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice_International_Airport" title="KoÅ¡ice International Airport">KoÅ¡ice International Airport</a> is an airport serving <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="KoÅ¡ice">KoÅ¡ice</a>. It is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in Slovakia. The <a href="/wiki/Poprad%E2%80%93Tatry_Airport" title="PopradâTatry Airport">PopradâTatry Airport</a> is the third busiest airport, the airport is located 5&nbsp;km west-northwest of ski resort town <a href="/wiki/Poprad" title="Poprad">Poprad</a>. It is an airport with one of the highest elevations in Central Europe, at 718 m, which is 150 m higher than <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck_Airport" title="Innsbruck Airport">Innsbruck Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Slia%C4%8D_Airport" title="SliaÄ Airport">SliaÄ Airport</a> is the smallest international airport and currently operates only summer charter flights to popular sea resort destinations. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Railways_of_Slovak_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Railways of Slovak Republic">Railways of Slovak Republic</a> provides railway transport services on national and international lines. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bratislava" title="Port of Bratislava">Port of Bratislava</a> is one of the two international <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">river ports</a> in Slovakia. The port connects Bratislava to international boat traffic, especially the interconnection from the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Main%E2%80%93Danube_Canal" title="RhineâMainâDanube Canal">Rhine-Main-Danube Canal</a>. Additionally, tourist boats operate from Bratislava's passenger port, including routes to <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn" title="DevÃ­n">DevÃ­n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and elsewhere. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Port_of_Kom%C3%A1rno&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Port of KomÃ¡rno (page does not exist)">Port of KomÃ¡rno</a> is the second largest port in Slovakia with an area of over 20 hectares and is located approximately 100&nbsp;km east of Bratislava. It lies at the confluence of two rivers - <a href="/wiki/The_Danube" class="mw-redirect" title="The Danube">the Danube</a> and <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="VÃ¡h">VÃ¡h</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Slovakia" title="Tourism in Slovakia">Tourism in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Slovakia" title="List of castles in Slovakia">List of castles in Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Slovakia" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Slovakia">List of World Heritage Sites in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg/220px-Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg/330px-Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg/440px-Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Bojnice_SK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bojnice_Castle" title="Bojnice Castle">Bojnice Castle</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia features natural landscapes, mountains, <a href="/wiki/List_of_caves_in_Slovakia" title="List of caves in Slovakia">caves</a>, medieval <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Slovakia" title="List of castles in Slovakia">castles</a> and towns, folk architecture, spas and <a href="/wiki/Ski_and_winter_sports_in_Slovakia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ski and winter sports in Slovakia">ski resorts</a>. More than 5,4 million tourists visited Slovakia in 2017, and the most attractive destinations are the capital of <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">High Tatras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Most visitors come from the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (about 26%), Poland (15%) and Germany (11%).<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia contains many castles, most of which are in ruins. The best known castles include <a href="/wiki/Bojnice_Castle" title="Bojnice Castle">Bojnice Castle</a> (often used as a filming location), <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1_Castle" title="SpiÅ¡ Castle">SpiÅ¡ Castle</a>, (on the UNESCO list), <a href="/wiki/Orava_Castle" title="Orava Castle">Orava Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Castle" title="Bratislava Castle">Bratislava Castle</a>, and the ruins of <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="DevÃ­n Castle">DevÃ­n Castle</a>. <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cachtice_Castle" title="Äachtice Castle">Äachtice Castle</a> was once the home of the world's most prolific female serial killer, the 'Bloody Lady', <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_B%C3%A1thory" title="Elizabeth BÃ¡thory">Elizabeth BÃ¡thory</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG/220px-Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG/330px-Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG/440px-Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bardejov10Slovakia6.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The centre of <a href="/wiki/Bardejov" title="Bardejov">Bardejov</a> â a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Slovakia's position in Europe and the country's past (part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> monarchy and <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>) made many cities and towns similar to the cities in the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>), <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>) or <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>). A historical centre with at least one square has been preserved in many towns. Large historical centers can be found in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="TrenÄÃ­n">TrenÄÃ­n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="KoÅ¡ice">KoÅ¡ice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica" title="BanskÃ¡ Å tiavnica">BanskÃ¡ Å tiavnica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levo%C4%8Da" title="LevoÄa">LevoÄa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">Trnava</a>. Historical centres have been going through a restoration in recent years. </p>
      <p>Historical churches can be found in virtually every village and town in Slovakia. Most of them are built in the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> style, but there are also many examples of <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic architecture</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_Bystrica" title="BanskÃ¡ Bystrica">BanskÃ¡ Bystrica</a>, Bardejov and <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1sk%C3%A1_Kapitula" title="SpiÅ¡skÃ¡ Kapitula">SpiÅ¡skÃ¡ Kapitula</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St._James,_Levo%C4%8Da" title="Basilica of St. James, LevoÄa">Basilica of St. James</a> in LevoÄa with the tallest wood-carved altar in the world and the Church of the Holy Spirit in <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDehra" title="Å½ehra">Å½ehra</a> with medieval <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">frescos</a> are UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>. The <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Concathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Martin's Concathedral">St. Martin's Concathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> served as the <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> church for the Kingdom of Hungary. The oldest sacral buildings in Slovakia stem from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravian</a> period in the 9th century. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg/220px-Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg/330px-Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg/440px-Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2856" data-file-height="1904"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jasn%C3%A1_Ski_Resort_-_gondola_lift_Kosodrevina_-_Chopok_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cable cars at <a href="/wiki/Jasn%C3%A1" title="JasnÃ¡">JasnÃ¡</a> in the Tatra Mountains.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Very precious structures are the complete wooden churches of northern and northern-eastern Slovakia. Most were built from the 15th century onwards by <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a> and members of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">eastern-rite</a> churches. </p>
      <p>Tourism in <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak Republic">Slovak Republic</a> is one of the main sectors of the economy, but not using its whole capacity. It is based on internal tourism, where Slovaks spend holidays within the country. Major areas are: <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry" title="VysokÃ© Tatry">VysokÃ© Tatry</a>. To other regions belong: <a href="/wiki/Pieniny" title="Pieniny">Pieniny</a> National Park, MalÃ¡ Fatra NP, and <a href="/wiki/N%C3%ADzke_Tatry" class="mw-redirect" title="NÃ­zke Tatry">NÃ­zke Tatry</a> NP. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Castles and chÃ¢teaux
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>There are many castles located throughout the country. To the biggest and the most beautiful ones belong: <a href="/wiki/Bojnice_Castle" title="Bojnice Castle">Bojnice Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1_Castle" title="SpiÅ¡ Castle">SpiÅ¡ Castle</a>, StarÃ¡ Ä½ubovÅa Castle, <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%A1sna_H%C3%B4rka_Castle" title="KrÃ¡sna HÃ´rka Castle">KrÃ¡sna HÃ´rka Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orava_Castle" title="Orava Castle">Orava Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn_Castle" title="TrenÄÃ­n Castle">TrenÄÃ­n Castle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Castle" title="Bratislava Castle">Bratislava Castle</a>. To the castle ruins belong <a href="/wiki/Beckov_Castle" title="Beckov Castle">Beckov Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="DevÃ­n Castle">DevÃ­n Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ari%C5%A1_Castle" title="Å ariÅ¡ Castle">Å ariÅ¡ Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pova%C5%BEsk%C3%BD_hrad" title="PovaÅ¾skÃ½ hrad">PovaÅ¾skÃ½ hrad</a> (castle), and <a href="/wiki/Stre%C4%8Dno_Castle" title="StreÄno Castle">StreÄno Castle</a>, where was filmed <a href="/wiki/Dragonheart" title="Dragonheart">Dragonheart</a> movie. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Caves
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>Caves opened for public are mainly located in Northern Slovakia. In the south-west of the country only JaskyÅa Driny is opened to the public. The most popular ones are: DobÅ¡insÃ¡ Ice Cave, DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ Ä¾adovÃ¡ cave, DemÃ¤novskÃ¡ jaskyÅa slobody, Belianska cave, and Domica cave. To the other caves which are opened belong OchtinskÃ¡ aragonitovÃ¡ cave, GombaseckÃ¡ cave, and JasovskÃ¡ cave. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Spa resorts
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>There are many spas throughout the whole country. The biggest and the most favorite center is <a href="/wiki/Pie%C5%A1%C5%A5any" title="PieÅ¡Å¥any">PieÅ¡Å¥any</a> spa, where a big portion of visitors come from The Gulf countries, i.e. <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>. To the other famous spas belong: BardejovskÃ© kÃºpele, TrenÄianske Teplice spa, TurÄianske Teplice spa, and Spa RajeckÃ© Teplice. There are many smaller ones: KÃºpele Å tÃ³s, KÃºpele ÄÃ­Å¾, KÃºpele Dudince, KovÃ¡ÄovÃ¡, KÃºpele Nimnica, KÃºpele SmrdÃ¡ky, KÃºpele LÃºÄky, and KÃºpele VyÅ¡nÃ© RuÅ¾bachy with treatments against schizophrenia. </p>
      <p>Typical souvenirs from Slovakia are dolls dressed in folk costumes, ceramic objects, crystal glass, carved wooden figures, ÄrpÃ¡ks (wooden pitchers), <a href="/wiki/Fujara" title="Fujara">fujaras</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Folk_instrument" title="Folk instrument">folk instrument</a> on the UNESCO list) and <a href="/wiki/Vala%C5%A1ka" class="mw-redirect" title="ValaÅ¡ka">valaÅ¡kas</a> (a decorated folk hatchet) and above all products made from <a href="/wiki/Husk" title="Husk">corn husks</a> and wire, notably human figures. Souvenirs can be bought in the shops run by the state organisation ÃÄ½UV (<i>Ãstredie Ä¾udovej umeleckej vÃ½roby</i>âCentre of <a href="/wiki/Folk_art" title="Folk art">Folk Art</a> Production). <i>Dielo</i> shop chain sells works of Slovak artists and craftsmen. These shops are mostly found in towns and cities. </p>
      <p>Prices of imported products are generally the same as in the neighbouring countries, whereas prices of local products and services, especially food, are usually lower. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science">Science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Slovak Academy of Sciences">Slovak Academy of Sciences</a> has been the most important scientific and research institution in the country since 1953. Slovaks have made notable scientific and technical contributions during history. Slovakia is currently in the negotiation process of becoming a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>. Observer status was granted in 2010, when Slovakia signed the General Agreement on Cooperation<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> in which information about ongoing education programmes was shared and Slovakia was invited to various negotiations of the ESA. In 2015, Slovakia signed the European Cooperating State Agreement based on which Slovakia committed to the finance entrance programme named PECS (Plan for the European Cooperating States) which serves as preparation for full membership. Slovak research and development organizations can apply for funding of projects regarding space technologies advancement. Full membership of Slovakia in the ESA is expected in 2020 after signing the ESA Convention. Slovakia will be obliged to set state budget inclusive ESA funding. </p>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_density_in_Slovakia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Population_density_in_Slovakia.png/300px-Population_density_in_Slovakia.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Population_density_in_Slovakia.png/450px-Population_density_in_Slovakia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Population_density_in_Slovakia.png/600px-Population_density_in_Slovakia.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="530"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_density_in_Slovakia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population density in Slovakia. The two biggest cities are clearly visible, Bratislava in the far west and KoÅ¡ice in the east.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population is over 5.4 million and consists mostly of <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>. The average population density is 110 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> According to the 2011 census,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> the majority of the inhabitants of Slovakia are <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a> (80.7%). <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">Hungarians</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">ethnic minority</a> (8.5%). Other <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> include <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> (2%),<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a> (0.6%), <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">Rusyns</a> (0.6%) and others or unspecified (7.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-gov-stats_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-stats-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018 the <a href="/wiki/Median_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Median age">median age</a> of the Slovak population was 41 years.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The largest waves of Slovak emigration occurred in the 19th and early 20th centuries. In the 1990 US&nbsp;census, 1.8&nbsp;million people self-identified as having Slovak ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak language</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Slovak_language" title="History of the Slovak language">History of the Slovak language</a>
      </div>
