       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovak_alphabet.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/200px-Slovak_alphabet.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/300px-Slovak_alphabet.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/400px-Slovak_alphabet.png 2x" data-file-width="446" data-file-height="387"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovak_alphabet.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak alphabet">Slovak alphabet</a> has 46 characters, of which 3 are <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">digraphs</a> and 18 contain <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> is <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic language family</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> is widely spoken in the southern regions, and <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">Rusyn</a> is used in some parts of the Northeast. <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">Minority languages</a> hold co-official status in the municipalities in which the size of the minority population meets the legal threshold of 15% in two consecutive censuses.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia is ranked among the top EU countries regarding the knowledge of foreign languages. In 2007, 68% of the population aged from 25 to 64 years claimed to speak two or more foreign languages, finishing 2nd highest in the European Union. The best known foreign language in Slovakia is <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> report also shows that 98.3% of Slovak students in the upper secondary education take on two foreign languages, ranking highly over the average 60.1% in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> survey from 2012, 26% of the population have knowledge of <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at a conversational level, followed by <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> (22%) and <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> (17%).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The deaf community uses the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Sign_Language" title="Slovak Sign Language">Slovak Sign Language</a>. Even though spoken Czech and Slovak are similar, the Slovak Sign language is not particularly close to <a href="/wiki/Czech_Sign_Language" title="Czech Sign Language">Czech Sign Language</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Slovakia" title="Religion in Slovakia">Religion in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Levo%C4%8Da_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg/190px-Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg/285px-Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg/380px-Levo%C4%8Da_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Basilica of St. James in <a href="/wiki/Levo%C4%8Da" title="LevoÄa">LevoÄa</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala,_Ko%C5%A1ice,_Slovensko.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg/190px-D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg/285px-D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg/380px-D%C3%B3m_sv%C3%A4tej_Al%C5%BEbety_a_Kaplnka_sv._Michala%2C_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Slovensko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6011" data-file-height="3482"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/St._Elisabeth_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Elisabeth Cathedral">St. Elisabeth Cathedral</a> in KoÅ¡ice is Slovakia's largest church
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Slovakia" title="Constitution of Slovakia">Slovak constitution</a> guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>. In 2011, 62.0% of Slovaks identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholics</a>, 5.9% as <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a>, 1,8% as <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinists</a>, 3.8% as <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Slovak Greek Catholic Church">Greek Catholics</a>, 0.9% as <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox</a>, 13.4% identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> or non-religious, and 10.6% did not answer the question about their belief.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 2004, about one third of the church members regularly attended church services.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Slovak Greek Catholic Church">Slovak Greek Catholic Church</a> is an Eastern rite <a href="/wiki/Sui_iuris" title="Sui iuris">sui iuris</a> Catholic Church. Before World War&nbsp;II, an estimated 90,000 Jews lived in Slovakia (1.6% of the population), but most were murdered during the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>. After further reductions due to postwar <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">emigration</a> and assimilation, only about 2,300 Jews remain today (0.04% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 18 state-registered religions in Slovakia, of which 16 are Christian, one is Jewish, and one is the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith">BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hukelova_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hukelova-137">[137]</a></sup> In 2016, a two-thirds majority of the Slovak parliament passed a new bill that will obstruct <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and other religious organisations from becoming state-recognised religions by doubling the minimum followers threshold from 25,000 to 50,000; however, Slovak president <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Kiska" title="Andrej Kiska">Andrej Kiska</a> vetoed the bill.<sup id="cite_ref-Hukelova_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hukelova-137">[137]</a></sup> In 2010, there were an estimated 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> in Slovakia representing less than 0.1% of the country's population.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Slovakia is the only member state of the European Union without a mosque.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Slovakia" title="Education in Slovakia">Education in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Comenius_University_in_Bratislava" class="mw-redirect" title="Comenius University in Bratislava">Comenius University</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a>, coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, currently ranks <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Slovakia" title="Education in Slovakia">Slovak secondary education</a> the 30th in the world (placing it just below the United States and just above Spain).<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Education in Slovakia is compulsory from age 6 to 16. The education system consists of elementary school which is divided into two parts, the first grade (age 6â10) and the second grade (age 10â15) which is finished by taking nationwide testing called Monitor, from Slovak language and math. Parents may apply for social assistance for a child that is studying on an elementary school or a high-school. If approved, the state provides basic study necessities for the child. Schools provide books to all their students with usual exceptions of books for studying a foreign language and books which require taking notes in them, which are mostly present in the first grade of elementary school. </p>
      <p>After finishing elementary school, students are obliged to take one year in high school. </p>
      <p>After finishing high school, students can go to university and are highly encouraged to do so. Slovakia has a wide range of universities. The biggest university is <a href="/wiki/Comenius_University" title="Comenius University">Comenius University</a>, established in 1919. Although it's not the first university ever established on Slovak territory, it's the oldest university that is still running. Most universities in Slovakia are public funded, where anyone can apply. Every citizen has a right to free education in public schools. </p>
      <p>Slovakia has several privately funded universities, however public universities consistently score better in the ranking than their private counterparts. Universities have different criteria for accepting students. Anyone can apply to any number of universities. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Slovakia" title="Culture of Slovakia">Culture of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folk_tradition">Folk tradition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Folk tradition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Slovakia" title="Music of Slovakia">Music of Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Slovakia" title="Architecture of Slovakia">Architecture of Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vlkolinec_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vlkolinec_02.jpg/220px-Vlkolinec_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vlkolinec_02.jpg/330px-Vlkolinec_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vlkolinec_02.jpg/440px-Vlkolinec_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3844" data-file-height="2572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vlkolinec_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wooden folk architecture can be seen in the well-preserved village of <a href="/wiki/Vlkol%C3%ADnec" title="VlkolÃ­nec">VlkolÃ­nec</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Folk_tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk tradition">Folk tradition</a> has rooted strongly in Slovakia and is reflected in literature, music, dance and architecture. The prime example is a Slovak national anthem, <i>"<a href="/wiki/Nad_Tatrou_sa_bl%C3%BDska" title="Nad Tatrou sa blÃ½ska">Nad Tatrou sa blÃ½ska</a>"</i>, which is based on a melody from <i>"<a href="/wiki/Kopala_studienku" title="Kopala studienku">Kopala studienku</a>"</i> folk song. </p>
      <p>The manifestation of Slovak folklore culture is the "<i>VÃ½chodnÃ¡</i>" Folklore Festival. It is the oldest and largest nationwide festival with international participation,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> which takes place in <a href="/wiki/V%C3%BDchodn%C3%A1" title="VÃ½chodnÃ¡">VÃ½chodnÃ¡</a> annually. Slovakia is usually represented by many groups but mainly by SÄ½UK (<i>SlovenskÃ½ Ä¾udovÃ½ umeleckÃ½ kolektÃ­vâSlovak folk art collective</i>). SÄ½UK is the largest Slovak folk art group, trying to preserve the folklore tradition. </p>
      <p>An example of wooden folk architecture in Slovakia can be seen in the well-preserved village of <a href="/wiki/Vlkol%C3%ADnec" title="VlkolÃ­nec">VlkolÃ­nec</a> which has been the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pre%C5%A1ov_Region" title="PreÅ¡ov Region">PreÅ¡ov Region</a> preserves the world's most remarkable folk wooden churches. Most of them are protected by Slovak law as <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a>, but some of them are on the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> list too, in BodruÅ¾al, Hervartov, LadomirovÃ¡ and RuskÃ¡ BystrÃ¡. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes,_Sanok_2010_97.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG/220px-Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG/330px-Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG/440px-Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes%2C_Sanok_2010_97.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carpathian_Bazaar_of_Tastes,_Sanok_2010_97.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a> wearing <a href="/wiki/Folk_costume" title="Folk costume">folk costumes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Slovakia" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Slovakia">Eastern Slovakia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The best known Slovak hero, found in many folk <a href="/wiki/Mythologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Mythologies">mythologies</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Juraj_J%C3%A1no%C5%A1%C3%ADk" title="Juraj JÃ¡noÅ¡Ã­k">Juraj JÃ¡noÅ¡Ã­k</a> (1688â1713) (the Slovak equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a>). The legend says he was taking from the rich and giving to the poor. JÃ¡noÅ¡Ã­k's life was depicted in a list of literary works and many movies throughout the 20th century. One of the most popular is a film <i>JÃ¡noÅ¡Ã­k</i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Fri%C4%8D" title="Martin FriÄ">Martin FriÄ</a> in 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St._James,_Levo%C4%8Da,_Main_altar,_2017_v2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg/220px-St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg/330px-St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg/440px-St._James%2C_Levo%C4%8Da%2C_Main_altar%2C_2017_v2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3701" data-file-height="3171"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St._James,_Levo%C4%8Da,_Main_altar,_2017_v2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Main altar in the Basilica of St. James, crafted by <a href="/wiki/Master_Paul_of_Levo%C4%8Da" title="Master Paul of LevoÄa">Master Paul of LevoÄa</a>, 1517. It is the tallest wooden altar in the world.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Visual_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual art">Visual art</a> in Slovakia is represented through <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">drawing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Printmaking" title="Printmaking">printmaking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illustration" title="Illustration">illustration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handicraft" title="Handicraft">arts and crafts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a> or <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_art" title="Conceptual art">conceptual art</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Slovak_National_Gallery" title="Slovak National Gallery">Slovak National Gallery</a> founded in 1948, is the biggest network of galleries in Slovakia. Two displays in Bratislava are situated in <a href="/wiki/Esterh%C3%A1zy_Palace_(Bratislava)" title="EsterhÃ¡zy Palace (Bratislava)">EsterhÃ¡zy Palace</a> (<i>EsterhÃ¡zyho palÃ¡c</i>) and the Water Barracks (<i>VodnÃ© kasÃ¡rne</i>), adjacent one to another. They are located on the Danube riverfront in the Old Town.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_City_Gallery" title="Bratislava City Gallery">Bratislava City Gallery</a>, founded in 1961 is the second biggest Slovak gallery of its kind. It stores about 35,000 pieces of Slovak international art and offers permanent displays in <a href="/wiki/Johann_P%C3%A1lffy_Palace" title="Johann PÃ¡lffy Palace">PÃ¡lffy Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirbach_Palace" title="Mirbach Palace">Mirbach Palace</a>, located in the Old Town. Danubiana Art Museum, one of the youngest art museums in Europe, is situated near <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cunovo" title="Äunovo">Äunovo</a> waterworks (part of <a href="/wiki/Gab%C4%8D%C3%ADkovo_-_Nagymaros_Dams" class="mw-redirect" title="GabÄÃ­kovo - Nagymaros Dams">GabÄÃ­kovo Waterworks</a>). Other major galleries include: <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Andy Warhol Museum of Modern Art">Andy Warhol Museum of Modern Art</a> (Warhol's parents were from <a href="/wiki/Mikov%C3%A1" title="MikovÃ¡">MikovÃ¡</a>), <a href="/wiki/East_Slovak_Gallery" title="East Slovak Gallery">East Slovak Gallery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Zmet%C3%A1k_Art_Gallery" title="Ernest ZmetÃ¡k Art Gallery">Ernest ZmetÃ¡k Art Gallery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zvolen_Castle" title="Zvolen Castle">Zvolen Castle</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Slovak_literature" title="Slovak literature">Slovak literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Slovak_authors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Slovak authors">List of Slovak authors</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/130px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/195px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/260px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1236" data-file-height="1743"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_%C5%A0t%C3%BAr" title="Ä½udovÃ­t Å tÃºr">Ä½udovÃ­t Å tÃºr</a>, the author of the Slovak language standard
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Christian topics include poem <a href="/wiki/Proglas" title="Proglas">Proglas</a> as a foreword to the four <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospels</a>, partial translations of the Bible into <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a>, <i>Zakon sudnyj ljudem</i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Medieval_literature" title="Medieval literature">Medieval literature</a>, in the period from the 11th to the 15th centuries, was written in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, Czech and Slovakised Czech. Lyric (prayers, songs and formulas) was still controlled by the Church, while epic was concentrated on legends. Authors from this period include <a href="/wiki/Johannes_de_Thurocz" title="Johannes de Thurocz">Johannes de Thurocz</a>, author of the <a href="/wiki/Chronica_Hungarorum" title="Chronica Hungarorum">Chronica Hungarorum</a> and Maurus, both of them Hungarians.<sup id="cite_ref-Phillips_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phillips-146">[146]</a></sup> The worldly literature also emerged and chronicles were written in this period. </p>
      <p>Two leading persons codified the Slovak language. The first was <a href="/wiki/Anton_Bernol%C3%A1k" title="Anton BernolÃ¡k">Anton BernolÃ¡k</a> whose concept was based on the western Slovak <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialect</a> in 1787. It was the codification of the first-ever literary language of Slovaks. The second was <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_%C5%A0t%C3%BAr" title="Ä½udovÃ­t Å tÃºr">Ä½udovÃ­t Å tÃºr</a>, whose formation of the Slovak language took principles from the central Slovak dialect in 1843. </p>
      <p>Slovakia is also known for its polyhistors, of whom include <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Jozef_%C5%A0af%C3%A1rik" title="Pavel Jozef Å afÃ¡rik">Pavol Jozef Å afÃ¡rik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Bel" title="Matthias Bel">Matej Bel</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Koll%C3%A1r" title="JÃ¡n KollÃ¡r">JÃ¡n KollÃ¡r</a>, and its political revolutionaries and reformists, such <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Å tefÃ¡nik">Milan Rastislav Å tefÃ¡nik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dub%C4%8Dek" title="Alexander DubÄek">Alexander DubÄek</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Slovak_cuisine" title="Slovak cuisine">Slovak cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Slovak_wine" title="Slovak wine">Slovak wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_Slovakia" title="Beer in Slovakia">Beer in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Halusky_kapustnica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/220px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/330px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/440px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Halusky_kapustnica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Halu%C5%A1ky" title="HaluÅ¡ky">HaluÅ¡ky</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bryndza" title="Bryndza">bryndza</a> cheese, <a href="/wiki/Sourkrawt" class="mw-redirect" title="Sourkrawt">kapustnica</a> soup and ZlatÃ½ BaÅ¾ant dark beerâexamples of Slovak cuisine
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional Slovak cuisine is based mainly on <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a> is the most widely eaten, followed by <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">duck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">goose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey_as_food" title="Turkey as food">turkey</a>), <a href="/wiki/Flour" title="Flour">flour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Milk_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Milk products">milk products</a>. It is relatively closely related to <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_cuisine" title="Hungarian cuisine">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_cuisine" title="Czech cuisine">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_cuisine" title="Polish cuisine">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_cuisine" title="Austrian cuisine">Austrian cuisine</a>. On the east it is also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_cuisine" title="Ukrainian cuisine">Ukrainian</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Lemkos" title="Lemkos">Lemko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">Rusyn</a>. In comparison with other European countries, <a href="/wiki/Game_(hunting)" title="Game (hunting)">"game meat"</a> is more accessible in Slovakia due to vast resources of forest and because hunting is relatively popular.<sup id="cite_ref-EuropeNations2000_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuropeNations2000-147">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boar" class="mw-redirect" title="Boar">Boar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venison" title="Venison">venison</a> are generally available throughout the year. <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">Lamb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goat</a> are eaten but are not widely popular. </p>
      <p>The traditional Slovak meals are <a href="/wiki/Bryndzov%C3%A9_halu%C5%A1ky" title="BryndzovÃ© haluÅ¡ky">bryndzovÃ© haluÅ¡ky</a>, bryndzovÃ© pirohy and other meals with potato dough and <a href="/wiki/Bryndza" title="Bryndza">bryndza</a>. Bryndza is a salty cheese made of sheep milk, characterised by a strong taste and aroma. BryndzovÃ© haluÅ¡ky especially is considered a national dish, and is very commonly found on the menu of traditional Slovak restaurants. </p>
      <p>A typical soup is a <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a> soup ("kapustnica"). A <a href="/wiki/Black_pudding" title="Black pudding">blood sausage</a> called "krvavnica", made from any parts of a butchered pig is also a specific Slovak meal. </p>
      <p>Wine is enjoyed throughout Slovakia. <a href="/wiki/Slovak_wine" title="Slovak wine">Slovak wine</a> comes predominantly from the southern areas along the Danube and its tributaries; the northern half of the country is too cold and mountainous to grow grapevines. Traditionally, white wine was more popular than red or rosÃ© (except in some regions), and <a href="/wiki/Sweetness_of_wine" title="Sweetness of wine">sweet wine</a> more popular than dry, but in recent years tastes seem to be changing.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Beer (mainly of the <a href="/wiki/Pilsener" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilsener">pilsener</a> style, though <a href="/wiki/Dunkel" title="Dunkel">dark lagers</a> are also consumed) is also popular. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Slovakia" title="Sport in Slovakia">Sport in Slovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Sporting activities are practised widely in Slovakia, many of them on a professional level. <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> have traditionally been regarded as the most popular sports in Slovakia, though <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitewater_slalom" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitewater slalom">whitewater slalom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a> are also popular. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Ice Hockey
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/220px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/330px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/440px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Slovakia men's national ice hockey team">Slovak national ice hockey team</a> celebrating a victory against <a href="/wiki/Swedish_national_men%27s_ice_hockey_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish national men's ice hockey team">Sweden</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>One of the most popular team sports in Slovakia is <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. Slovakia became a member of the <a href="/wiki/IIHF" class="mw-redirect" title="IIHF">IIHF</a> on 2 February 1993<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> and since then has won 4 medals in <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">Ice Hockey World Championships</a>, consisting of 1 gold, 2 silver and 1 bronze. The most recent success was a silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/2012_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2012 IIHF World Championship">2012 IIHF World Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>. The Slovak national hockey team made five appearances in the Olympic games, finishing 4th in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>. The country has 8,280 registered players and is ranked 7th in the <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_Ranking" title="IIHF World Ranking">IIHF World Ranking</a> at present. Before 2012, the Slovak team <a href="/wiki/HC_Slovan_Bratislava" title="HC Slovan Bratislava">HC Slovan Bratislava</a> participated in the <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">Kontinental Hockey League</a>, considered the strongest hockey league in Europe, and the second-best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slovakia hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2011 IIHF World Championship">2011 IIHF World Championship</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Finland_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Finland men's national ice hockey team">Finland</a> won the gold medal and <a href="/wiki/2019_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2019 IIHF World Championship">2019 IIHF World Championship</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Finland_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Finland men's national ice hockey team">Finland</a> also won the gold medal. Both competitions took place in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="KoÅ¡ice">KoÅ¡ice</a>. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Football
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tehelne_pole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tehelne_pole.jpg/220px-Tehelne_pole.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tehelne_pole.jpg/330px-Tehelne_pole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tehelne_pole.jpg/440px-Tehelne_pole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4656" data-file-height="2620"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tehelne_pole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Football stadium <a href="/wiki/Teheln%C3%A9_pole" title="TehelnÃ© pole">TehelnÃ© pole</a> in Bratislava. Football is the most popular sport in Slovakia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Football is the most popular sport in Slovakia, with over 400,000 registered players. Since 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak national football team">Slovak national football team</a> has qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> once, in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a>. They progressed to the last 16, where they were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a>. The most notable result was the 3â2 victory over <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>. In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak national football team">Slovak national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> tournament, under head coach <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Koz%C3%A1k_(footballer,_born_1954)" title="JÃ¡n KozÃ¡k (footballer, born 1954)">JÃ¡n KozÃ¡k</a>. This helped the team reach its best-ever position of 14th in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>. </p>
      <p>In club competitions, only three teams have qualified for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> Group Stage, namely <a href="/wiki/MFK_Ko%C5%A1ice" class="mw-redirect" title="MFK KoÅ¡ice">MFK KoÅ¡ice</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1997â98 UEFA Champions League">1997â98</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Artmedia_Bratislava" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Artmedia Bratislava">FC Artmedia Bratislava</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2005â06 UEFA Champions League">2005â06 season</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M%C5%A0K_%C5%BDilina" title="MÅ K Å½ilina">MÅ K Å½ilina</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010â11 UEFA Champions League">2010â11</a>. FC Artmedia Bratislava has been the most successful team, finishing 3rd at the Group Stage of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Cup" title="2005â06 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>, therefore qualifying for the knockout stage. They remain the only Slovak club that has won a match at the group stage. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><style
